Current Affairs Commentary

A New Posture in China's Foreign Trade 11

— Zi

At the end of last month, the Customs announced the news that the trade surplus in December of last year was more than five million yuan. Yesterday, newspapers published the news that the trade surplus in January of this year was more than one million and three hundred thousand yuan. From the perspective of China, which has been in a state of trade deficit for many years, regardless of whether the reason is a positive phenomenon affected by the new monetary policy or a negative phenomenon indicating the weakness of national purchasing power, it is an event that cannot but be noted. Since the establishment of Customs import and export trade statistics in our country, except for the record of a rare trade surplus of more than 270,000 taels of customs duties in the third year of Tongzhi (1864), the trade deficit in taels of customs duties in other years has been as high as more than 556 million (Republic of China 21) and as low as more than 16 million (Republic of China 8). This trade deficit occupies an extremely important position in China's international balance of payments. In other words, it is a major loophole in China that has been worried by those who study China's economic problems but have no way to reverse it. Now, trade surplus reports have been seen twice in a row. Although the numbers are small, from the perspective of creating a new posture in Sino-foreign trade, the relationship is quite important. Now, let's investigate it based on the facts.

First, the trend of China's trade deficit increased most sharply in the five years from the 17th to the 21st years of the Republic of China. In the 22nd year, the trend changed to a decline. It is estimated that the 22nd year decreased by more than 130 million yuan compared with the previous year, and the 23rd year decreased from 70 million yuan in the previous year to 50 million yuan. Last year, it decreased to more than 340 million yuan. According to this observation, even if trade surplus reports are not often seen in the coming months of this year, the amount of trade deficit must be greatly reduced compared with the past. This can be known from the trend in the past three years.

Second, there is one thing to note in the above-mentioned trend, that is, the annual decrease in the trade deficit is directly proportional to the decrease in the total trade volume. Many say that the reason why the total trade volume figure is low is partly due to the decline in the prices of imported and exported goods, and partly due to the decline in trade. Considering that the exports in January were more than 37 million yuan and the imports were more than 35 million yuan, each not reaching the level of 40 million yuan for monthly trade deficit during the peak trade season, it is still difficult for the Chinese to decide whether to worry or rejoice today.

Third, in the trade surplus phenomenon of the past two months, tung oil ranks first in exports. In the past, China's export goods were mainly soybeans, silk, tea, eggs, cotton, leather, and silk. Tung oil failed to rank among the top ten in the 20th and 21st years of the Republic of China, and only suddenly ranked fifth in the 22nd year. It is gratifying that this item has been newly added to China's export trade, but at the same time, the decrease in exports of silk and tea is also a cause for concern. This should also be paid attention to.

According to the above three observations, China's foreign trade has its own hopes for revitalization in the implementation of this new monetary policy. However, how to enable the large-scale export of important domestic products to meet the world's needs and benefit people's livelihoods still requires effort. Otherwise, the establishment of this new posture of trade surplus is actually gratifying but not yet gratifying.

Germany's Three-Step Response to the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact Observe Paris's Movements Before Deciding Course of Action Preparations Made Long Ago for Military Occupation of the Rhineland 12

Berlin: Hitler is keeping silent about what reaction Germany intends to make to the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact in the future. Hitler has now gone to his villa in the Bavarian mountains to rest. German political circles are of course very concerned about the pact, but the general public believes that Germany's decision on this matter will be entirely decided by its leader. Before the results of the French Senate's debate on the pact are known, Hitler intends to take a wait-and-see approach. If the French Senate approves it and does not make any concessions to Germany's concerns, then Hitler may take one of the following three steps: Send troops to march into the Rhineland demilitarized zone with flags flying and drums beating. Publicly announce that Germany is no longer legally bound by the demilitarization of the Rhineland, but believes that Germany's political power in the area is now sufficient to protect everything, pending a solution to the matter by international regulations. Submit a serious protest to France, reserving Germany's right to make a final decision on this matter. The first step seems unlikely to be realized, because Hitler does not want to anger world opinion as a result. Moreover, because the occupation of the Rhineland area is no longer a problem, German military experts have long been prepared inside and outside the area and can occupy and defend it within 24 hours. There is ample evidence of this. (23rd Reuters Dispatch)

British Planning Ahead for Developments in Far East and Europe Defence Reorganisation Plan White Paper Soon to Be Tabled in Parliament 13

London: The government's white paper on the defence reorganisation plan will be tabled in the House of Commons for debate next week, when Foreign Secretary Eden will give a report on the current international situation. The diplomatic correspondent of The Observer has been speculating on the upcoming parliamentary session and what Foreign Secretary Eden may say: "Since Germany's vigorous rearmament plan has achieved great success and Japan's militaristic policy of external expansion in the Far East has been making progress day by day, the current diplomatic situation has become increasingly serious. There is no doubt that Foreign Secretary Eden will repeatedly clarify this point when explaining the necessity of the UK's defence reorganisation plan. In addition, Eden will explain that the UK also needs to reorganise its defence in order to cope with the situation in Eastern Europe. In principle, the UK has a responsibility to guarantee Austria's independence. Considering the recent visit of German Aviation Minister and Prussian Governor-General Goering to Poland and the active propaganda campaign promoted by German Envoy to Austria von Papen in Vienna (the purpose of which is to induce Yugoslavia to break away from the Little Entente and reach an understanding with Austria), it can be seen that there are many hidden dangers in Eastern Europe and the urgency of the problem is obvious." (23rd Havas Dispatch)

Senator Borah Broadcast Speech Criticizing British Policy 14

Washington: Republican Senator Borah gave a broadcast speech on Washington's Birthday today, saying that there is cunning propaganda overseas against the US neutrality policy in the Italo-Ethiopian War, and the initiator of this propaganda is actually the UK. When Japan invaded Manchuria, the UK remained neutral for its own benefit, but now, because the African war is related to its own interests, it has adopted a non-neutral policy. Although it is acting with discretion, the UK has its own considerations. However, if the UK criticises the US for adopting a neutral policy in the Italo-Ethiopian War or any other disputes in Europe, and regards it as an act of supporting war or pursuing selfish and immoral claims, then the UK or any other country should not have this right. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

Italy Hopes Countries Will Lift Sanctions Unwilling to Remain on Sidelines Regarding European Affairs No Agreement Possible Without Italian Cooperation Negotiations Impossible Without Lifting Sanctions 15

Rome: Recently, there have been rumours that the Italian government intends to take advantage of the fact that the political issues of the naval conference have not yet been resolved to demand negotiations to lift sanctions as a condition for accepting future naval agreements. A semi-official spokesperson recently made a statement to the press on this issue: "Any international agreement cannot be established without Italy, and Italy can never remain on the sidelines of European affairs. This is obvious from the current situation. If countries want to ostracise Italy from the European community by means of sanctions, and then, when they need Italy's help, they demand its cooperation, especially on the issue of the Danube River Convention and the three issues of the Locarno Pact (which are Italy's responsibility). This is simply absurd." According to our correspondent, regarding the issue of the conclusion of a convention by the countries of the Danube River basin, the Italian government informally stated during the talks in Paris at the beginning of the month that any agreement without Italy's participation will never be realised. However, as long as the sanctions against Italy are in effect, Italy will not be able to hold negotiations with the countries implementing the sanctions. Later, when Foreign Minister Suvich of Italy and Austrian Foreign Minister Guido Schmidt met in Florence, Schmidt said that most of the elements of the Danube River Convention are already in place, and the conclusion can be expected. He hoped that Italy would change its negative attitude to facilitate the realisation of the convention. At that time, Suvich insisted on the above-mentioned position in response to Schmidt. As for the issue of the naval agreement, semi-official sources here believe that among the four powers participating in the naval conference, the UK is most concerned about the future naval agreement. It is willing to conclude even a partial agreement. However, it is rumoured that unless the sanctions are lifted or Italy receives at least some guarantee, it will not sign the future naval agreement and assume any obligations. However, this claim has recently been denied by semi-official sources. Regarding the issues of the Locarno Pact, semi-official sources believe that this is not a new issue at present. However, regarding the conflict between the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance treaty and the Locarno Pact, Italy and Germany share similar views. According to our correspondent, after the German Ambassador to Italy, Hasell, met with Suvich, he rushed back to Berlin to discuss the relationship between the Franco-Soviet treaty and the Locarno Pact with the German leader, Hitler. He has now completed his mission and returned to his post. (23rd Havas Dispatch)

500,000 Italian Army Soldiers Granted Indefinite Leave Claims of Dismissal Denied They May Be Recalled at Any Time 16

Rome: Rumours that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has decided to dismiss 500,000 soldiers, nearly half of the Italian army, due to the gradual improvement of the European situation have been denied here today. According to reliable sources, the soldiers will be granted indefinite leave but may be recalled at any time. At the same time, the government announced that the Supreme Military Council will meet tomorrow. (22nd National Society Dispatch)

New Naval Treaty Arms Reduction Becomes Arms Expansion Opens the Door for Unlimited Shipbuilding Competition Limit on Gun Calibre a Mere Formality Fortifications in the Pacific No Longer Prohibited 17

London: If the London Naval Conference can conclude a treaty to replace the previous London and Washington treaties, its contents will be largely disappointing. The outline of the treaty, according to well-informed sources speaking to the Associated Press, is largely predictable. In short, it will open the door to unlimited naval competition. However, those who advocate the treaty will still call it a way to reduce international distrust, because Existing treaties stipulate that countries building warships must notify other countries when the keel is laid. The new treaty stipulates that notification must be given one year in advance. The new treaty will reduce the existing gun calibre limits in several clauses. The new treaty will announce a suspension of the construction of large cruisers. However, critics still believe that The new treaty does not limit the number of ships or total tonnage, leading to unlimited competition. Even the gun calibre limit is a mere formality, because it will not be effective if countries outside the treaty exceed this limit. Fortifications in the Pacific are no longer prohibited. Efforts to reduce the tonnage and power of battleships over the years have been abandoned. At the same time, observers here believe that Japan will greatly increase the construction of submarines, destroyers and small cruisers in the future. (22nd National Society Dispatch)

Careful Consideration of Wording of Naval Treaty UK and France Propose Alternative Compromise 18

London: Regarding the issue of inviting non-participating countries to the naval conference to sign and join the future agreement, the UK originally advocated that each signatory country entrust the UK to hold talks with non-participating countries, including Germany, which was rejected by France. The experts of the two countries will formulate alternative compromises and draft a protocol to specify the conditions and deadlines for inviting non-participating countries to sign and join the agreement this autumn. This morning, the experts of the two countries held talks to discuss the wording of this naval conference protocol. The British representatives were Clay, a naval expert from the Foreign Office, and Malkin, a legal advisor from the Foreign Office. The French side was represented by Peng Gu (son of the current Minister without Portfolio, Peng Gu). No agreement was reached and it was decided to consult again on Sunday. (22nd Havas Dispatch)

US Insists on Original Position on Battleship Tonnage Issue 19

London: Regarding the issue of battleship tonnage, France recently asked the US whether it could be reduced. According to sources from the French side, Norman Davis, the chief US representative to the naval conference, replied to French Chief Representative, Ambassador Corbin, this morning. However, the US delegation denied this news, saying that the US will not submit a reply to France through diplomatic channels, and it is still unknown now. Moreover, after France raised this question to the US, the delegations of the two countries held talks, at which time the US reiterated that the figure of 35,000 tons should remain unchanged. (22nd Havas Dispatch)

US Undersecretary of the Navy Dies of Illness 20

WASHINGTON - Undersecretary of the Navy Henry Roosevelt died of heart disease today. Roosevelt was a distant relative of President Roosevelt. He graduated from the Naval Academy in 1900. During the Spanish-American War, he served on the battleship "Mayflower," patrolling the coast of Cuba. In 1914, he was a naval attache at the American Embassy in Paris. After the outbreak of the European War, he was transferred back to Washington. He then left the Navy until March 1933, when he was appointed Undersecretary of the Navy. (National News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

After the Japanese General Election, the Okada Cabinet's Position is Consolidated; The Minseito Party Decides to Fully Support the Diet; The Military Advocates Reforming the Cabinet to Cope with Extraordinary Times 21

TOKYO - The Minseito Party, which surged from 126 to 205 seats, is naturally not satisfied with the positions of Commerce Minister Machida and Education Minister Kawazaki. Therefore, it may ask Prime Minister Okada to find an opportunity to consider reforming the cabinet, which is a central issue in the future political situation and deserves attention. However, the Minseito Party executives gathered last night to exchange views on this issue. As a result, they believe that in this critical period, the whole country must unite to overcome the difficulties. As for taking advantage of the victory to reform the cabinet, such an action is unacceptable in terms of the party's credibility. They must still strive to assist Prime Minister Okada, further consolidate the situation under the control of Commerce Minister Machida, and properly manage the situation. This opinion has been unified. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

TOKYO - The military believes that the results of the general election show that the Minseito Party has become the largest party, and the proletarian parties have also made great progress. This shows that the people hope that the whole country will unite to break the current situation and seek reform in this extraordinary period. Therefore, the government must respect public opinion and decide to reform the cabinet, welcoming representatives from the Seiyukai Party and the proletarian parties, who are in opposing positions, to form a truly united cabinet to cope with the extraordinary domestic and foreign situation and move towards the implementation of national policies. Minister of the Army Kawashima will advise Prime Minister Okada based on this opinion. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

TOKYO - Regarding the results of the general election, the financial community initially believed that no matter which party, the Seiyukai or the Minseito, won, the fiscal and economic policies would not undergo drastic changes given the current situation. Therefore, they did not pay much attention. However, some people still believed that if the Seiyukai Party won, fiscal policy might undergo some changes, which caused some anxiety. Now that the election results show that the Minseito Party has won an absolute majority, the political situation can be said to be gradually stabilizing. However, the great progress of the Minseito Party also implies that the issue of cabinet reform is brewing. It is fully conceivable that the current cabinet will become Minseito-colored. However, with Finance Minister Takahashi still in office, there should be no changes in policy. The implementation of the eleventh-year budget will generally adhere to the policy of gradually reducing public debt and exercising compilation. Therefore, the financial and industrial circles can generally maintain calm. The financial community absolutely supports the maintenance of Takahashi's financial policies, and the financial community is therefore very relieved that the government has won. At this opportunity for a new division in the political arena, the financial community hopes that the government will actively implement policies to stabilize the people's livelihood and strive to adjust relations between China and Japan. I am deeply pleased that this general election has been completed peacefully. The government can only respect the will of the people expressed in this way, move forward on the path it believes in, and strive to improve international relations and expand national power. Easing of Japanese-Russian Situation

Legal Federation Considers Withdrawing Troops from the Far East, Agrees to Organize a Joint Committee to Handle Russian-Manchurian Border Disputes 25

MOSCOW - A certain foreign dignitary here recently expressed his opinion to our reporter, saying that the relations between Japan and Russia are no longer as tense as before. On the Russian side, in particular, they want to promote a further easing. Therefore, the proposal to withdraw a portion of the troops stationed on the Siberian border can also be considered. The railway transportation reform project in Siberia will soon be completed. At that time, Soviet troops can be transported quickly no matter where they are heading to the border. Therefore, reducing the number of troops stationed on the border does not cause any obstruction. According to reliable sources, the Mongolian troops stationed on the "Manchukuo" border have already retreated inland in order to avoid incidents. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

MOSCOW - According to our reporter's investigation, Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Stomoniakov recently held talks with Japanese Ambassador to Russia Ota (Ota held consultations with Foreign Minister Litvinov on the 15th and 16th of this month). The discussion focused on the organization of a Russian-"Manchu"-Japanese tripartite committee to handle the recent Russian-"Manchu" border affairs. The Soviet side originally advocated the appointment of commissioners of other nationalities to participate in the matter. It is now heard that this claim has been abandoned, and it has been agreed with Japan that the duty of the commission is limited to investigating the conflict in the Krotekov area on January 30. The investigation results may only be reported to the governments of Russia, "Manchu," and Japan and have no right to judge right or wrong. The number of commissioners dispatched by the three parties is equal, and all will be filled by military officers, who will be appointed from the troops that did not participate in the Krotekov area conflict. However, the number of commissioners and the date of the meeting have not yet been decided because Japan still has to wait for the Soviet Union to submit a reply. Insiders here believe that the establishment of this commission is experimental in nature. Once successful, Japan and Russia may establish several more joint committees to handle various outstanding issues between Russia, "Manchu," and Japan. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

MOSCOW - Ambassador Ota visited Deputy Foreign Minister Stomoniakov at the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs on the afternoon of the 21st. As a result of the consultation on the establishment of an investigation committee for the Jinchanggou incident, the participation of commissioners from third countries was excluded. The mixed commissioners were composed only of representatives from Japan, "Manchu," and the Soviet Union to conduct on-site investigations. The two sides agreed on this opinion. Although the details of the organization, the number of commissioners, and the schedule of meetings have not yet been decided, the number of commissioners from Japan, "Manchu," and the Soviet Union are equal, and military personnel other than those involved in the case will be appointed as commissioners to report the situation of the investigation to the three governments separately for final consultations. (Domei dispatch, 21st)

TOKYO - Regarding the establishment of a joint investigation committee to handle the Jinjanggou incident, Ambassador Ota held talks with the Soviet Foreign Ministry on the 21st. The contents of the talks were telegraphed to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 23rd. It is said that the committee did not recognize the participation of third-country nationals, and it was composed of commissioners from Japan, "Manchu," and the Soviet Union with an equal number of commissioners from each side. The two sides agreed. In the near future, they will hold further consultations to decide on the details of the investigation of the dispute. The determination of the number of commissioners and their qualifications must also await negotiations between Japan and the Soviet Union. It seems that each side will send three commissioners, but it still needs to be agreed upon between Japan and "Manchu." The Japanese side advocates that the Deputy Consul in Suifenhe, Chuzin, and the Kwantung Army and "Manchukuo" each select one commissioner. As for the parties involved in the dispute between Japan, "Manchu," and the Soviet Union, they will participate as referents. In addition, a similar fact-finding committee must also be established on the Manchurian-Mongolian border, but there is no report on the points raised by the Soviet side. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 21st)

A Glimpse of Italy in Wartime (Part 1) - The Third Observation of the European Situation Under the Shadow of Killing Intent 27

— By Lonis Fisher, Translated by Bin Fu

Yesterday I came from the snowy Alps to the temperate climate of Lombardy. Today I strolled around the streets for a long time. Every shop used the colors of the national flag, green, white, and red, to display signs that said "This shop only sells Italian goods." There was also a kind of sign that advised people to only buy Italian goods or products from non-sanctioning countries. A pharmacy announced that "Patriotic Italians only buy Italian medicine." A coffee shop warned drinkers to "Only drink Italian wine." Some of the slogans also quoted fragments from Mussolini's speeches. If the sanctions were strictly enforced, this kind of patriotic voluntary action would probably be endless. This anti-sanction propaganda is meant to incite a deep hatred of foreigners among the people and concentrate them under the Fascist group.

Books about East Africa, Abyssinia, and black races are piled up in bookstores. In the window of every bookstore, there is a special display of the book "Britain's Conquest in Africa" by Karevanli, because the Italians often repeatedly retort: "Britain itself has looted so much in Africa, what right does she have to interfere with our conquest of Abyssinia?" Of course, she has no right to interfere; but morality is inherently unimportant in imperialist policy.

The glass window of a stationery store was covered with postcards and pictures. One of the postcards for sale showed an Italian officer in tropical uniform. He faced a group of Abyssinian chiefs, some kneeling before him, and some standing upright giving him the Roman salute. Below this was the notation in brackets: "Enemies." Behind him, a hand holding a long sword was about to slash him in the back. The long sword was labeled with the word "Sanctions." Below this was also a small note in brackets: "Our friends." I also saw in many places a postcard depicting an armed Italian soldier trampling on a map of Abyssinia. He held a torch in his hand, burning in the three colors of green, white, and red. On this colored flame was written the Italian word Civilita (Civilization).

"Give gold and iron to the motherland." On a certain street, I saw a freight truck parked in front of a coffee and tea shop. The crowd watched as a brown-shirted man stuffed empty coffee cans onto the truck. The truck box was already full of scrap iron and broken tin. A magazine sold at a newsstand had a cartoon print on it, showing a ship carrying gold about to leave the port. This was "The Escape of Gold from France." Behind this picture was another picture showing Italians throwing earrings, rings, gold watches, and similar things into the furnace. This was "The Golden Gifts Received by Italy."

Photographs of Mussolini are everywhere - Mussolini is angry, frowning, pouting, smiling; Mussolini is drawing his sword, shooting, swimming, pacing and speaking, playing the piano; Mussolini is on a cannon, on a tank, on a horse, on a platform; Mussolini is simple, wearing a Roman crown, a steel helmet, a Fascist cap; Mussolini, Mussolini. He has a dramatic flair that Italians love. His eyes flash with a fanatical ferocity. His heavy, protruding jaw shows strength and will; his contracted lips tell of a world-shocking ambition.

Sometimes I wandered into the poorer areas of Milan, and I couldn't help but think of my childhood. Because the smell I smelled here was the same as the smell in the Italian area of ​​South Philadelphia where I grew up. I remember that my Italian playmates were bold, noisy, and brave. Our young "gang" often pushed coal trains, and everyone threw coal at each other. But Italian children are not the best soldiers.

In a more remote part of Milan, I saw some old announcements from the Milan Provincial Government, which said in essence that "In order to support the central government's grand event," a cash prize of 300 names was specially set up, each with 500 lire (Lire is the name of Italian currency) to mothers who can raise three children between October 28, 1931 and October 28, 1936. The notice stated that priority was given to poorer families. I assert that no one will want to participate in this competition. Having to have three children in five years! The Fascist Party just wanted to use this as an excuse to say that overpopulation made Abyssinia necessary for them. At the same time, they are doing their best to exaggerate the problem of overpopulation. The daily newspaper publishes official statistics every day. According to today's evening paper, the number of births in Milan last month was 1,197; deaths 967; marriages 627. An Italian propaganda publication once said, "The status of women under Fascist rule is actually the center of the family." But she "must have fulfilled her sacred mission, ... she must be a mother" - especially if she can encourage her sons to become soldiers.

Today is Sunday, and I ran to the magnificent marble chapel. Here are two thousand marble statues, some located on very high minarets; here are carved glass windows; here are beautiful and solemn ceremonies and singing. In the square outside, the black-shirted band played patriotic hymns. One or two people in the crowd applauded each verse.

I wandered into a precious showroom. A huge map of Abyssinia made of transparent material hung on the wall. Behind it, in the space from Addis Ababa to the Sudanese border, was embedded Mussolini's helmeted head, flickering brightly and dimly. Nearby, a mechanical bee was sucking nectar from a flower in a very orderly manner.

On the avenues, side streets, and on the walls of all the buildings, every gap was filled with slogans. "Mussolini", "Long live Duce", "Long live the Conqueror of Adowa", "Long live the Fascist Revolution, Long live the Glorious Army of East Africa, Long live My Emperor," this also long live, that also long live. Everywhere again were brown posters of Mussolini's helmeted head. I noticed that many of the slogans had been torn. Some were torn off a corner or a strip with fingers. Some were cut a hole in the center with a sharp weapon. This made me very interested. I walked street after street. Many of the slogans on the central streets were only torn. Some of the slogans on the remote streets were simply torn off completely. I looked at the advertising posters, but they were rarely torn off, and most of them were still intact. I hired a car to go to the suburbs, and then strolled back slowly. If this phenomenon of tearing slogans has political significance, I can be sure of my observations. There is no doubt about it: with very few exceptions, the Fascist slogans were torn off by the hands of planned saboteurs. There are fewer slogans in the suburbs of Milan than in the city, but occasionally a few have been torn off.

The Danube River Convention Issue: Czech-Yugoslav Talks are Harmonious 30

After that, he returned to the city and held a second political talk with Stoyadinovich at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He then had lunch together. After the meal, he continued to meet. Once Hodza and Stoyadinovich hold a third meeting, they will no longer continue to meet. Hodza is scheduled to meet with reporters and foreigners at 6:45 PM today. According to well-informed sources, the relationship between the two countries was extremely harmonious during the talks. (Havas Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Charcoal Train's Satisfactory Trials in Paris; Highly Valued by the Government 32

PARIS - The government recently tested a new engine on a train from Paris to Chartres. The engine uses charcoal as fuel. The results of the test were excellent. The speed was 190 kilometers per hour, and the cost of fuel was only 0.14 francs per horsepower per hour. This test has a close relationship with the problem of liquid fuel substitutes currently being studied by the "French Scientific Research Institute." After this test, it proves that charcoal engines are fully capable of being used in the transportation industry. The government attaches great importance to this new invention. This is enough to be seen by the personal participation of the Minister of Agriculture, the Minister of Public Works, and the authorities of the National Defense Agency in the test drive. It is natural that the Public Works Department attaches importance to this matter. The Ministry of Agriculture is also concerned about it, because this new invention can give an important sales channel for domestic timber. The National Defense Agency also pays attention to it, because once this method is popularized, countries that lack oil will not be restricted by foreign oil imports. Although the use of charcoal as fuel for engines is not new, this is the first time it has been used in trains. Last autumn, the government tested charcoal cars in Landes (a famous wood-producing area in the south). The speed was very low, which is far different from the 190 kilometers per hour of trains. This shows that this new invention has made progress. In addition, because the train engine is larger in size, it stores more charcoal than cars. As a result, the locomotive can complete a longer route without adding fuel in the middle. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

German Historical Geographer to Release Newly Compiled Historical Map of China; Available This Summer 33

BRAUNSCHWEIG, GERMANY - German Herman, Professor of Historical Geography at the University of Berlin, completed the "Historical Fact and Map of China" at the request of the Harvard-Yenching Institute of Massachusetts, USA. This map has been submitted to the famous map printing company Weimann for publication. When this map was being made, it was originally intended to include various Chinese, Japanese, and European characters. However, when comparing and studying various maps, the materials to be enriched were still lacking. Therefore, the materials taken for the new map are also quite extensive, covering the writings of Turkish, Arabic, Brazilian, Greek, Roman, and modern experts, all of which are included in the reference. There are 112 pages in the map, and the scale and text size are the same for comparison. Those who are interested in Chinese issues here all believe that after the map is published this summer, it will become a standard Chinese map and an unprecedented masterpiece. It is heard that a modern Chinese map will be published soon. (National News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

Geography Lecture: Why Do We Study Foreign Geography? 71

— Huang Guozhang, Head of the Geography Department, Central University

Whether in junior high school or high school, foreign geography is a required course. I think everyone must have a question in their minds, which is, why do we study foreign geography? The answer to this question is, of course, different for everyone, but in my personal opinion, there are three main reasons why we need to study foreign geography:

First, to understand the interrelationships between nations.

Second, to understand China's position in the international arena.

Third, to serve as a model for improving national welfare and people's livelihoods.

Regarding the first point, studying foreign geography can help us understand the interrelationships between nations. Now, I will first discuss several basic elements of international relations and their relationship with geography, and then give a few examples to illustrate that a country's external relations all have their own special geographical background.

The world today is like an organism, with each part having a mutually interconnected effect. No part is unaffected by the outside, and no part cannot affect the outside. The saying "pull one hair and move the whole body" is enough to show the depth of current international relations. Standing in the world today, it is not only those in power who need to have a deep understanding of the interrelationships between nations and the major issues between nations, but also the general public should have a preliminary understanding of the international situation in order to serve as a backing for the country's diplomatic negotiations. Only in this way can so-called citizen diplomacy be realized one day.

The current international situation has reached an extremely serious and complex point. Many countries feel that political problems are difficult to solve; many countries feel that society is unstable; the majority of countries are suffering from economic panic and cannot live in peace; and many countries are being invaded by international capital imperialism and are in dire straits, unable to find a way out in politics, economics, and society. The interests of each country and the serious problems they face are different, which makes the interrelationships between nations even more complicated.

Although the interrelationships between nations are complex, the formation of this complex international relationship has five basic elements. If we want to have a reasonable understanding of this complex international relationship, we must start with these five basic elements that make up international relations. Now, I will simply explain them one by one:

Exclusive ownership of land and natural resources — Almost everywhere on the earth, except for the newly discovered areas of Antarctica, is managed by a country, and most of the land and natural resources are privately owned. If a country wants to expand its territory or add to its natural resources, it simply has no other opportunity than to infringe upon the land and natural resources owned by other countries. Places that were originally not very relevant are also connected for this reason.

Rapid population growth and uneven distribution — Before the 18th century, the world had only 400 to 500 million people, equivalent to China's current population. According to the latest statistics, the total world population has reached about 2 billion. The number of people added in a short period of two or three hundred years has exceeded four or five times the number of people added since humans first existed, which is truly a miracle in the history of human population growth. The rapid increase in population in recent centuries is due to the development of modern science, which has increased human production capacity and increased the average lifespan. However, there is no limit to population growth, while the area of land and natural resources in the world are finite, and the increase in productivity also has a certain limit. Therefore, the major countries of the world are almost universally suffering from the panic of overpopulation and are eagerly trying to occupy places with relatively sparse populations in order to make plans for emigration abroad, or to forcibly seize the resources of weak countries in order to increase the living resources of their own populations. The international disputes caused by this are countless.

The world's population is not only increasing rapidly, but also very unevenly distributed. Many places have less than two people per square mile, while many places have more than a thousand people per square mile. Southeast Asia, Northwestern Europe, and the northeastern part of the United States are all extremely densely populated areas in the world, with an average of more than 200 people per square mile. In these places, the competition for human survival is extremely intense. Some rely entirely on good weather and abundant harvests to barely make a living each year, while others rely entirely on peace and tranquility, with no wars, and raw materials and manufactured goods can be transported and circulated everywhere to barely survive. If the weather is bad, the harvest is poor, or international trade declines for some reason, many people will feel the danger of hunger and cold, and the whole world will feel uneasy.

Uneven distribution of natural resources — Mineral resources are the foundation of modern new-style industries, but the distribution of mineral resources is very uneven among the countries of the world. For example, for coal needed to develop heavy industry, four-fifths are produced in the United States, Germany, and the United Kingdom; for the iron needed, three-quarters are produced in the United States, France, and the United Kingdom; for petroleum, more than nine-tenths are produced in the United States, Mexico, and Russia; three-quarters of the copper are produced in the United States, Chile, and Japan; and three-quarters of the gold are produced in South Africa, the United States, and Canada. In addition, other mineral resources are also concentrated in a small number of countries. The uneven distribution of mineral production and the level of utilization of natural resources and the amount of production costs in each country are, of course, very important, but the biggest reason is the uneven distribution of mineral deposits themselves. Some places have a lot, some places have little, and mineral deposits are formed naturally, which cannot be changed by human power. Less is less, more is more, and people can do nothing about it. Moreover, mineral resources are natural wealth created over many past eras, and one ton is used up, so one ton is gone. It is absolutely impossible to remedy this. However, the need for various mineral resources is not limited to one country or one place, and at the same time, the minerals produced in one country or one place may not be completely consumed by that country or that place. Under these circumstances, the only solution is for various places to help each other, transporting their surplus to other places and importing what is lacking from other places. In this way, the interdependent relationship between the countries of the world is deeper, and international problems become more complex. This is only in terms of mineral resources; other agricultural products, manufactured goods, etc., are also subject to local restrictions and require cooperation between various regions. In other words, they can all promote the closer relationship between nations.

Improvement of transportation — The progress of modern science has made human transportation methods more and more ingenious day by day, and the distance on the earth is shortening day by day. In the past, people sighed at the ocean, but now they can travel around the world by steamship. Railways and highways can climb mountains and cross ridges, and airplanes and airships can even fly over the high sky. Land cables and submarine cables are densely distributed on the earth, and radio can use the ether in the air to communicate information between various places. The so-called "the ends of the earth are like neighboring villages" is really not an exaggeration from today's perspective. The exchange of ideas or goods everywhere in the world is very convenient, and the relationship between nations is becoming closer.

Due to the improvement of transportation and the convenience of transportation, the sources of materials needed for our daily lives have expanded even more, and the development of international trade has seen a rapid increase. Just think about the food, clothing, and things we use at home, and how many of them are transported from foreign countries. China is known as an agricultural country, but it is not self-sufficient in food and needs to import large quantities of rice from Annam, Siam, and other places every year. Clothing materials are also insufficient and need to import large quantities of cotton from India and large quantities of cotton cloth from Japan. The steel machinery needed for construction projects and the gasoline and vehicles needed for highways are mostly imported from foreign countries. As for daily utensils, the number of items imported from foreign countries is countless. If the cotton harvest in India is poor, the price of cotton in Shanghai and Osaka will rise, and the price of cotton yarn and cotton cloth will increase, and our clothing will become more expensive. If Annam and Siam experience unexpected floods or droughts, the price of rice in Shanghai will rise. This is only in terms of China; the situation in other countries is even more extreme. Due to the relationship of international trade, the whole world can be said to have become a whole economic unit.

The impact of the Industrial Revolution — Since the United Kingdom first raised the banner of the Industrial Revolution at the end of the 18th century, countries around the world have been affected by it one after another, using the power of machinery and underground coal and iron to promote the development of human industrial life, engaging in mass production, and wanting to find a new way out for human survival from industry. The biggest result of the Industrial Revolution is, on the one hand, the massive increase in manufactured goods, and on the other hand, the massive increase in the consumption of raw materials and fuels. The massive amount of manufactured goods cannot be consumed by one country or one place, and the massive amount of raw materials and fuels cannot be supplied by one country or one place. It is necessary to find markets for manufactured goods and supply bases for raw materials and fuels elsewhere. Imperialism has risen from this point, international trade has developed from this point, and the interrelationships between nations have become even more complex.

The above are the five basic elements that make up the current complex international relationship. If you want to have a reasonable understanding of international relations, you must start with these basic elements. But if you want to have a reasonable understanding of these basic elements, you must first have a reasonable knowledge of foreign geography. Which of the so-called distribution of the world's population and the living conditions of the people, the distribution of natural resources, the distribution of transportation routes, and the situation of commodity transactions in various places is not a matter of geography? Therefore, the occurrence of every international problem has a profound geographical background. Geographical knowledge can be said to be the key to solving international problems. This is the first purpose of why we need to learn foreign geography. (To be continued)

Page 9

Records of Life in the Borderlands (10) 72

— Jin Dui

12. The Yunting Canal and Resettlement Measures in Ningxia

Ningxia's water conservancy is the most famous in China. The network of canals is intricate, as described in previous articles. However, within the borders of Ningxia and Lingwu, there are still fields that cannot be irrigated by the existing canals. In particular, the western bank of the Yellow River near Ningxia County is a vast, flat expanse of fertile land, yet the population is sparse, with few villages. This abundant source of wealth has become a desolate wasteland. To alleviate the irrigation difficulties of the former and to develop the barren land of the latter, the provincial authorities should select a site between Ningxia and Lingwu counties to build a new canal; this is both a plan and a necessity.

This planned canal project has indeed been implemented. Because it is entirely built by military engineers, the construction costs are very low. From the winter of the 23rd year to the spring of last year, the project continued, being interrupted or progressing depending on the weather. Finally, on May 11th of the 24th year, the Yunting Canal held its water opening ceremony.

The construction of this canal, including the dikes and bridges along the way, allocated over 120,000 yuan. The canal is about 120 li long and irrigates an area of about 600,000 mu. It is named "Yunting Canal" in memory of General Ma Fuqun (zi Yunting), former chairman of the enemy suppression.

Although the canal is complete, many fields in the irrigated area remain barren. If no measures are taken to cultivate them, the benefits of repairing and constructing the canal will not be significant. Therefore, after the completion of the canal, a resettlement plan is needed. It is said that the construction costs of the canal were over 120,000 yuan, with a surplus of 70,000 to 80,000 yuan. The provincial authorities plan to use the remaining funds from the canal project, plus the registration fees collected during the land survey, totaling about 200,000 yuan, as resettlement expenses. The plan is to first resettle 400 to 500 households to establish three new villages and cultivate the barren land on both sides of the canal. The origin of the resettled people, whether from within or outside the province, is not restricted. In the future, as cultivation develops, local construction will be undertaken. Adding 500,000 to 600,000 mu of land out of nowhere and increasing the population will ensure that the fruits of the canal's benefits are abundant.

In the 24th year administrative plan of the Ningxia Provincial Government, under the "Cultivation" section of construction projects, there is a "Yunting Canal Area Reclamation Method."

"After the opening of the newly built Yunting Canal in Ningxia, tens of thousands of mu of land can be irrigated. It is planned to establish a Yunting Canal Area Reclamation Preparation Office to implement military-civilian reclamation. The methods are as follows: (A) The Reclamation Preparation Office will be composed of the staff office and adjutant of the 15th Route Army Headquarters, one specialist in cultivation, one section chief from the Construction Department, and one officer in charge of the reclamation troops. The matters to be handled are as follows: surveying and mapping the reclamation area; examining the geology of the reclamation area; designing and constructing residential areas, fortresses, dikes, bridges, roads, and dredging ditches; implementing land leveling and regional division; allocating residential areas, cultivated mu, farm tools, livestock, seeds, fertilizers, etc.; handling immigration matters. (B) Measure tens of thousands of mu of land as a reclamation area for a regiment. A regiment of officers and soldiers has 500 people, with 20 mu of land per person, totaling 30,000 mu of land. In addition, building houses, repairing canals, and building roads total 30,050 mu. The regiment's special service company, heavy artillery company, and three battalions, each with four companies, are four units. Each company has nine squads, with ten to twelve people per squad. One squad cultivates 200 mu of land, one company cultivates 2,000 mu of land, and four companies cultivate 8,000 mu of land, allocated in four corners. The middle is the battalion, and the middle of that is the regiment, entirely a military organization. The larger unit is based on the regiment, and the smaller unit is based on the squad. One squad lives in a fortress. The military organization is applied to the administrative organization, and the military and civilians are integrated, implementing the baojia system. One squad cultivates 200 mu of land, equivalent to the land cultivated by one jia of people. Nine squads are equal to one bao. Four bao are equal to one lianbao. Four lianbao are equal to one district, just as four battalions are equal to one regiment, which can house 1,500 households. All supplies and houses are made by the military. The vehicles and livestock are purchased by the government and will be repaid with the produce in the future. The production distribution method is public military production and public distribution. For 200 mu of land, 100 mu are planted with rice, and 100 mu are planted with wheat. After the wheat and rice are harvested, they are stored together in public warehouses. In addition to each family's consumption, the public uses the equipment, which is paid off in installments. The surplus is distributed according to diligence and laziness. All barren land will be cultivated by the military and then handed over to the people for cultivation."

The following is "Measures for Recruiting Immigrants." Recorded below: "Ningxia is located in the upper reaches of the Yellow River, at the strategic point of the Northwest. The land is fertile, and the water conservancy is convenient. Only the population is sparse, and the land is desolate. The border area feels empty, and the land advantage is not fully utilized. However, the southeastern provinces are narrow and densely populated, with no land to cultivate. The supply is often disrupted, and food shortages often cause panic. Now, to adjust the population, increase production, develop the land, a specific the Yunting Canal, Hezhongbao, Zhensupao, Ligangbao, Zima Beach, Guangwu, Yao Fubao and other places as resettlement areas, stipulating preferential measures for farmers, the connotations are as follows:

(A) Immigration procedures. All those who wish to immigrate to this province, whether as individuals or legal entities, shall obtain a license from their respective provincial or county government to prove their identity, and the issuing authority shall first notify the total number of men and women in the household, the date of departure, and the route to the provincial reclamation bureau for preparation. The selection of farmers, regardless of refugees, disaster victims, or farmers voluntarily immigrating, shall be qualified by good character, diligence, and hard work. It is especially appropriate for those who bring their families with them.

(B) Reception methods. Reclamation reception offices will be set up on the main roads to and from the border of this province. After farmers enter the territory of this province, they shall report with the certificate or license they carry in order to receive them. The addresses of the temporary reception offices are Guangxingyuan in Dengkou County, Zibao in Zhongning County, and Huianbao in Yanchi County.

(C) Placement measures. This government will set up reclamation sub-bureaus in designated reclamation areas, select suitable locations, and build a number of new villages. The village office will review the farmers' occupations, allocate residences, and allocate barren land according to the number of farmers. Each adult male will be granted 20 mu of land, and the elderly, young, and women will be granted half the amount."

Liu Zhenhua Inspects the Dikes in Anhui Province, The Construction Length Is Over 600 Kilometers, Chuan Ruling Also Inspects Various Dike Projects

Wuhu Correspondence: The good dikes along the Yangtze River in Anhui Province are Wangjiang, Susong, Huaining, Tongcheng, Wuwei, and Hexian on the north bank of the river, and Dangtu, Wuhu, Fanchang, Tongling, Guichi, and Dongliu on the south bank of the river, with a total length of over 1,000 kilometers. In recent years, they have suffered from floods many times. Each time, the dike body was not strong, and it was overflowing and collapsed, resulting in a major disaster, leading to rural bankruptcy and people fleeing. In view of this, the provincial government has specifically designated the regulation of water conservancy as the central work of this year. For inner counties, northern Anhui focuses on river channels, and southern Anhui focuses on ponds and dikes. Water conservancy supervisors are assigned to each administrative supervisory area, so as to be specifically responsible. After precise measurements of the river dikes, such as Laozhoutou, Biyang River, Mahua Dike, Guangji Dike, Yongle, Huangsitan, Mapu, and Baoda, the length of those that should be constructed and repaired reaches 644 kilometers. It is estimated that 7,326,920 cubic meters of earthwork are needed, and about 3,663,400 man-days are required. The project funds have been subsidized by the central government with 500,000 yuan of disaster relief public bonds. Other labor service and construction labor, and the county's requisition, have also obtained great assistance. Provincial Chairman Liu Zhenhua, in addition to ordering the county magistrates to assist in the work, also accompanied Construction Department Director Liu Yiyan and Construction Department Water Conservancy Section Director Wen Yi, on the 21st, took the Anfeng Chariot from Anqing, and inspected the dike project along the river. That night, they passed Wuhu and went straight down to Caishi to stay overnight. At 5 p.m. on the 22nd, they returned to Yan. Liu will inspect the upstream of Anqing, he is eager to travel as a relative, did not land, and immediately took the original transport back. Liu Yiyan and Wen Yi landed in Wuhu, because Fu Ruling, Chairman of the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Committee, also scheduled to depart from Beijing on the 23rd by survey ship, to inspect the entire Yangtze River dikes. Liu Yiyan intends to meet Fu and then accompany him to inspect the dike projects in Anhui Province. When Liu Zhenhua arrived in Wuhu, he announced the results of the inspection, that Wuwei and Huaining counties started construction earlier, and the dikes in these two counties were more important. All counties were ordered to start work on the same day and complete the work before the end of April, so as not to delay the busy farming season or prevent work from being harmed by the arrival of spring floods (22nd)

Last Year's Overseas Chinese Remittances to Xiamen Were Calculated To Be Over 11.6 Million, Which Was Only Enough To Offset Last Year's Import Surplus in Xiamen

Xiamen Correspondence: Overseas Chinese in various British, Dutch, American, and French territories in Southeast Asia are mostly from southern Fujian, so Xiamen port also accounts for the highest percentage of overseas Chinese remittances to China. The rise and fall of the economy in southern Fujian and the prosperity and decline of trade in Xiamen depend on this. Southern Fujian produces very little. It has been open to trade for 70 years and is an example of import surpluses. The most prosperous period was in the 18th and 19th years of the Republic of China, when imports reached 29 million to 30 million customs taels and exports were only 4 million taels. This huge import surplus also relied on overseas Chinese remittances to make up for it. In addition to making up for this import surplus, overseas Chinese remittances are also capital for purchasing property in their home country. The most prosperous period was when annual remittances reached 40 million to 50 million taels. After the 18th year of the Republic of China, the world economic panic affected Southeast Asia, and industries shrank. Fortunately, gold prices rose and exchange rates were extremely high. Overseas Chinese remitted funds back to Xiamen from the 19th to the 21st year of the Republic of China. However, there have been years of banditry in southern Fujian, the troops are everywhere, and they dare not invest in the interior. At that time, Xiamen opened up a new market, and housing prices rose, so they invested in Xiamen real estate. According to the Chamber of Commerce, the total amount of overseas Chinese capital invested in Xiamen real estate reached 80 million yuan. After the 21st year of the Republic of China, real estate values plummeted. The price of one land was 240,000 yuan, but now it is only 40,000 yuan, and no one cares. This fund has become stagnant in real estate. After the 22nd year, remittances have been greatly reduced. There were still 20 million yuan in the previous year. Last year (the 24th year), according to the Xiamen Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, which was released the day before yesterday, after two months of time, all Chinese and foreign banks, remittance bureaus, and folk post offices were investigated to obtain the exact number, totaling only 11,636,925 yuan. At the same time, customs statistics show that last year's trade surplus in Xiamen was 11,014,000 yuan (exports were 3,677,000 yuan), which was only enough to make up for the import surplus. However, the shrinkage of imports is less than one-third of that in the 18th and 19th years of the Republic of China. The speed of the decline in purchasing power is shocking. It can also be inferred that both southern Fujian and overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia have fallen into a deep abyss of depression (February 19)

Zhejiang Province Plans to Implement Cuttlefish Fishing Ban 74

Dinghai Correspondence: The dispute between net fishing and cage fishing of cuttlefish is an important issue in the fishing disputes between Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Zhejiang Jian intends to thoroughly resolve the situation. The Provincial Fisheries Experiment Field has studied the advantages and disadvantages of net fishing and the artificial culture of cuttlefish. The field has drafted fishing ban periods and measures, and submitted a request for implementation. The measures and explanations are summarized below: (Explanation of the principles and methods of cuttlefish fishing ban period and banning the scraping and drying of fishing cages)

"It has been found that the peak spawning period for cuttlefish is between May 15th and 16th. Before and after this time, although cuttlefish come to swim near the sea for reproduction, the number is very small and unimportant. The incubation situation of cuttlefish has been studied and the results show that eggs produced in May or early June require more than 30 days to hatch due to the low water temperature (about 17 to 20 degrees Celsius). Eggs produced after early June require 26 to 30 days to hatch due to the higher water temperature (about 19 to 22 degrees Celsius). It can be seen that the incubation of cuttlefish eggs is most common after June 16th until July 20th. This period can also be called the main period of fish egg incubation, and the fish eggs attached to the fish cage are most easily shaken off or damaged by the friction between the cage and the side of the boat, so that the fish eggs can be naturally incubated, so it is stipulated that after the fishing ban period, cage fishing is not only harmless, but also can help the reproduction of cuttlefish.

According to the field's experiments and investigations in the 24th year, it was found that the incubation of cuttlefish eggs is most common from late June to mid-July. If the fishing ban period is stipulated to be from June 20th to July 20th every year, cuttlefish will have a great opportunity to reproduce in large quantities, and there will be no great obstacle to fishing. At this time, it is near the end of the fishing season, and the fish are thin and weak after reproduction, and the quality is also poor, so prohibiting fishing will not affect the livelihood of fishermen.

It has also been found that there are four aspects of cage fishing and other fishing operations that harm the reproduction of cuttlefish and should be banned: Patting cages. Fishermen dislike that the fish cages have too many fish eggs attached to them. Every time they pick up the cage, they first take out the cuttlefish, and then pat the outside of the cage to make the fish eggs fall off and sink into the sea. This kind of treatment is enough to make the fish eggs have no chance to develop and should be banned. Sunning cages. During the fishing season, the fish cages have too many fish eggs attached to them, which hinders the effectiveness of fishing. Fishermen will carry the cages to the land and expose them to the hot sun, so that the fish eggs dry up and fall off, and then carry them back to the fishing grounds for use. Although this kind of behavior can give fishermen a temporary benefit, it is extremely harmful to the reproduction of cuttlefish and should also be banned. Burning cages. After the fishing season, the bamboo cages are heavy due to the fish eggs attached to them, and they are moldy and unbearable after being used for a long time. Fishermen often raise the cages, put them on the land, dry them, and use them as fuel. This action is of very little benefit to the fishermen, but it greatly hinders the development of fish eggs and should also be banned. Net fishing for juveniles. The current sea bream nets and large fishing nets used in the Zhoushan, Zhongjie Mountain, and Maanshan Islands are not intended to catch small cuttlefish, but because their mesh size is too small and the period of use is when the small cuttlefish have just hatched from the fish eggs and are drifting in the sea, therefore, a large number of juvenile cuttlefish often enter the net at the same time as other fish. This kind of net is very harmful to the natural reproduction of cuttlefish and should also be banned as soon as possible. However, the operation of sea bream nets and large fishing nets is closely related to the livelihood of fishermen, and a suitable ban cannot be determined without further detailed research.

In summary, based on the above principles, six measures can be drafted for the fishing ban period and banning the scraping and drying of fishing cages, as follows: First, the cuttlefish fishing ban period is set from June 20th to July 20th every year. During this period, all cage fishing or net fishing fishermen are prohibited from fishing. Second, all fish cages for catching cuttlefish should be left in the sea after June 20th and not allowed to be taken out for reuse. Third, it is not allowed to pat the cage when raising the fish cage during fishing. Fourth, fish eggs which have been put in the water must not be transferred to the land again. When eggs are attached to the cage in excess, the old cage mountain rope can be taken off and discarded into the sea, and the new cage can be reattached to the dry rope. Fifth, the above-mentioned fishing ban period and banning measures shall be implemented by personnel from the governments of each county in this province, the fisheries police bureau, and the construction department. If people find any violations of the above regulations, they must also report to the above-mentioned executive agencies at any time. Sixth, fishermen who violate the above regulations shall be fined more than five yuan and their fishing gear may be confiscated. Those who violate the regulations more than twice shall be punished with double fines and their fishing rights shall be revoked. The above six banning measures (the ban on catching small cuttlefish is intended to be studied further) are in line with the facts, and will not have a great impact on the livelihood of fishermen when implemented, and seem to be feasible, but people have shallow knowledge, and are accustomed to the customs, and may not be easy to implement for a while, so it is intended to propose setting up implementation areas to test the above measures. Before the trial implementation has yielded any results, the other locations will remain the same, so as to avoid fishing disputes. The fundamental cause of the cage and net fishing disputes lies in the conflict of interests of the fishermen (which has no relationship with the reproduction issue). The solution seems to be the exclusive fishing rights and fishing rights, so that one model and one net have a certain operating location, and there will be no conflict. On the other hand, regardless of cages and nets, they must be registered, so that the government can have perfect statistics, and the annual catch of cuttlefish can be clearly understood. The rise and fall of the industry will provide a basis for future administrative facilities, and the benefits will be great."

Letter to the Editor 80

To the esteemed editor of the *Shen Bao*:

I have read a news item on the third page of your newspaper on the 23rd, entitled "Taicang Party Department Sends Letter to County Education Bureau Director." Upon investigation, this does not match the facts. The meeting place that day was the Mass Education Center. Jin Cheng arrived at the center at 8:41 AM. At that time, County Party Committee member Huang Yinggong also arrived. After resting for about ten minutes and comparing the time, Director Zhou of the center inquired with the Taicang Bank and learned that it was exactly 9:00 AM. This shows that Jin Cheng's watch was not wrong. The statement that "the Education Bureau Director did not arrive until after 10:00 AM" is a false accusation. Furthermore, before the reading of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will, the master of ceremonies did not call for everyone to recite aloud along with the voice. However, the primary school students near the front of the stage, upon hearing the chairman's voice, immediately recited along with the voice according to their usual habits. Those standing behind were not prepared for this and followed along one after another, resulting in a lack of uniformity. Moreover, because the chairman's pronunciation location at the time was not at the front of the stage and he was not facing the audience, many in the audience could not clearly distinguish whether to respond or not. However, the meeting was orderly from beginning to end. This also shows that there was no so-called "omission of important words." Moreover, Jin Cheng has been a responsible person in education for many years, how could he not be able to recite the will? Some local newspapers have published rumors based on misinformation, and a letter has already been sent to correct them. The news in your newspaper is likely based on local newspapers. Jin Cheng is truly afraid that the rumors will become increasingly illusory, so he has sent a special letter requesting a correction.

Respectfully, Guan Jincheng, February 23rd, afternoon.

Special Article: A Commoner's View on Civilian Anti-Gas Defense (Continued) 81

— Xu Jun

Although on the battlefield, complete gasification is not easy due to the movement of the battle lines, in the city, it can be completely gasified by aerial attacks or artillery fire. However, if the citizens have adequate training and knowledge in gas defense, can calm their minds, and handle it calmly, there is nothing to fear. The purpose of using poison gas is not only to kill and injure the enemy's military and civilians, but also to undermine the enemy's morale, harm its order, and achieve both lethal and psychological effects.

6. Matters to Pay Attention to in Gas Defense

In the past two years, our authorities, in view of the tension in the international situation and the intensity of the great powers' war preparations, have held one or two air defense exhibitions and air defense exercises. At that time, many propaganda teams were organized to put up slogans along the streets, distribute leaflets, and give lectures on defense methods, instilling various kinds of knowledge, and providing much guidance to citizens on gas defense and air defense. The points that should be noted are briefly described below:

Selection of Personnel: (A) The personnel in charge of air defense and gas defense propaganda, organization, training, guidance, and other work should be mainly composed of air defense and gas defense specialists, but at a minimum, they must also be very knowledgeable in military science. (B) The materials for explanation or instruction must be well understood and explained in detail, so that citizens can thoroughly understand them. (C) With a military mindset, have a considerable assessment of the effectiveness of poison gas, but do not exaggerate it, so as not to scare citizens. (D) Use practical experience to explain defense methods, so that citizens will not panic when real poison gas comes, and can maintain order and tranquility. (E) The instructions for defensive equipment must be simple, economical, and convenient, and must not focus on one side.

Defense Methods: Individual defense equipment, gas masks are very good, but they are national weapons and cannot be issued to civilians at will. Moreover, in our country, which is economically stretched, the replenishment of gas masks for the national defense forces is still insufficient. If they are to be issued to the people, it is also difficult to do so in practice. If the people were to buy them, there is no large-scale manufacturing plant in our country to meet the needs of the citizens. Even if factories were established and manufactured in large quantities, our poor countrymen (each costing about twelve yuan) would find it difficult to prepare one each. Even the average middle-class citizen can prepare one, but the method of use and preservation must also be given considerable education and practice. In practice, it is best to adopt the following simple methods: (A) All effective poison gases are heavier than air and have the property of flowing downwards. The best defense is to run to a high place (such as climbing a building or going up a mountain). (B) The release of poison gas is greatly affected by the wind direction and has a tendency to flow with the wind. To avoid it, go to the left, right, or upwind. (C) Low-lying areas and alleys are places where poison gas accumulates, as they are not easily dissipated. Pay attention to avoiding them. (D) Poison gases with lethal properties take several hours or even days to take effect. If rescue is prompt, there is no danger. In such cases, go to a shelter or rescue station for treatment as soon as possible. (E) Tear gas is not life-threatening unless in extremely high concentrations. If you encounter it, close your eyes tightly. It will only take an hour at most. (F) Many poison gases decompose with water. Covering the mouth and nose with a wet towel can also defend against them. Even if the poison gas does not decompose with water, it can reduce the amount absorbed. (G) The method of group defense should be a gas-proof shelter, but it is also subject to economic constraints. For convenience, it is best to use the lower part of the building as a gas-proof shelter. However, most houses in our country, although wide and spacious, are made of flimsy materials and will be reduced to ashes in the event of a bombing. There are also many gaps in the tiles and walls, which are dangerous for leaking poison gas. Residential buildings in cities, on the other hand, are made of stronger materials, but there are very few that are suitable. To address the gas defense problem, the improvement of urban buildings should be the top priority. Appendix: The following are the conditions and precautions for shelters: 1. The renovation procedures are simple, easy to enter, and close to food storage. 2. Constructed tightly, with no easy entry for outside air. 3. The entrance and exit doors must have two layers, and be at least four feet apart (eight feet for rescue stations) so that two curtains are not opened at the same time when entering and exiting. The curtains must also be tightly installed. 4. Ordinary shells and bombs will not damage it, so the construction must be solid. 5. Since the air inside the shelter is isolated from the outside, and there are many people, there is of course a need for air supply, so there must be ventilation equipment. The air that is brought in must be filtered through a gas filter. The ventilation method can be manual or mechanical. 6. To prevent the intrusion of poison gas, the internal air pressure must be greater than the outside. 7. A layer of lime must be laid on the ground to absorb the carbon dioxide exhaled by people. 8. When leaving the shelter, the white (lime or bleaching powder) traces on the feet must be removed to avoid being detected by enemy aircraft.

7. Disinfection and Rescue

Disinfection methods are the responsibility of disinfection teams, but the public should also know the basics for temporary disposal. (A) Methods of disinfecting areas: (A) Burning method: If there is gas (except liquid) in an area, the burning method can be used to drive it out by expanding the volume of the gas. (B) Soil piling method: If there is liquid gas in an area, soil piling can be used to bury it. (C) Spraying method: If there is unstable gas in an area, water can be used to decompose it. (B) Methods of disinfecting equipment: (A) Blowing method: If equipment is contaminated with gas, it can be hung in a large wind opening and allowed to be blown to remove the gas. (B) Sunning method: If equipment is contaminated with gas, it can be placed in the sun to decompose the gas. (C) Boiling method: If equipment is contaminated with gas, it can be placed in boiling water to remove the gas by steam pressure. (D) Other items, such as utensils, that are contaminated with gas, can be rubbed with petroleum or volatile oil to disinfect them. (C) Methods of rescue: (A) Move the poisoned person to a safe place and do not subject them to excessive shocks. (B) Give them strong tea and coffee, as well as cardiac stimulants, to restore their spirits. (C) Keep them lying on their backs with a high pillow in fresh air, and give them oxygen when necessary, while maintaining their body temperature. (D) Quickly remove their clothes and give them new clothes, but do not shake them. (E) Seek medical help quickly.

8. Conclusion

Based on the above, poison gas is not a terrible thing, and defense, elimination, and rescue are also very convenient. In the event of a gas attack, the first thing to do is to be calm, act quickly, strictly observe discipline, respect order, and take appropriate action according to the situation. If not, the harm from being poisoned will be small, and the injury from trampling on each other will be great. In particular, the organization, training, and knowledge of our people are very immature, so special attention must be paid to strictly adhering to discipline and observing order.
