National Goldsmith Industry: Representative Assembly Opened in Shanghai Yesterday 82

Over 600 Representatives from Various Provinces, Cities, Counties, and Towns Attended

Resolution Passed to Form a Petition Group to Go to Beijing Tomorrow Evening

Requesting the Ministry of Finance to Revise Silver Usage Management Regulations

Yesterday, Shanghai's gold and silver industry, including 14 established firms, 16 newer firms, and 120 other related businesses, following the resolution of the preparatory meeting the day before, closed for one day. Each jewelry store displayed a sign stating: "Today, the national gold and silver industry is holding a joint assembly; closed for one day." Simultaneously, all workshops also ceased operations for one day. At 1:00 PM, a national gold and silver industry representative assembly was held in the grand hall of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Over 600 representatives from eleven provinces, including Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Shanxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Hebei, Shandong, and Fujian, and seven cities, including Shanghai, Tianjin, Beiping, Nanjing, Hankou, Qingdao, and Nanchang, including Gu Suming, Chuan Shengmao, and Cai Jilun, organized a petition group, passed a memorial, and decided to gather in Shanghai tomorrow evening to take the Beijing-Shanghai overnight express train to Beijing to petition the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to revise the management regulations regarding silver usage in silver products. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Representatives

Yesterday's attendees included representatives from eleven provinces: Hebei, Henan, Shandong, Jiangxi, Anhui, Sichuan, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian; and seven cities: Tianjin, Beiping, Nanchang, Nanjing, Qingdao, Hankou, and Shanghai; as well as representatives from various counties and towns such as Chongde, Lanxi, Huzhou, Huaiyin, Ningbo, Xuzhou, Wuxi, Wujin, Wuxian, Rugao, Dongtai, Jiangdu, Xinghua, Baoying, Bengbu, Wuwei, Jiaxing, Kunshan, Changshu, Yongjia, Haizhou, Banpu, Haimen, Jiangyin, and Changzhou, totaling over 600 people. Gu Suming from Zhejiang Province, Cai Jilun from Jiangsu Province, Chuan Shengmao from Shanghai, Ran Xizhang from Nanjing, and Zou Hexuan from Hankou were publicly elected as a five-member presidium. Zhou Renjie served as the master of ceremonies, and Cao Yazhou and Cheng Suiliang served as recorders.

Resolutions Passed

After formal greetings, Gu Suming first reported on the purpose of the meeting, followed by Chuan Shengmao's report on the preparatory process. Then, Ran Xizhang, Cai Jilun, Zou Hexuan, and others reported on the situations in various regions. Immediately afterward, discussions began. Regarding the proposal to request assistance from Du Yuesheng, Lin Kanghou, Yu Zuoting, and Yu Qiaqing, the resolution was passed. Regarding the organization of the petition group, the resolution was passed, following the preparatory meeting's decision to have each province and city send two to five representatives. Regarding welcoming voluntary participation in the petition, the resolution was passed. Regarding setting the date for the petition, the resolution was passed, setting the date for taking the night train to Beijing on Tuesday. At 5:30 PM that afternoon, they would gather at the guild hall, and on the 26th, they would petition the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance. Regarding the proposal to send written thanks to all sectors in the name of the assembly, the resolution was passed. Regarding revising the petition memorial, the resolution was passed. Regarding the fact that although the Ministry of Finance promulgated the silver usage management regulations on November 14th, this association only received the order on November 15th, and this should be corrected, the resolution was passed. Regarding presenting a memorial to the National Federation of Commerce requesting the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to revise the regulations to eliminate restrictions, the resolution was passed. Regarding the petition expenses being set at 1,000 yuan, to be temporarily advanced by the initiators, the resolution was passed. As for the petition representatives of the petition group, the registered representatives included Zou Hexuan from Hankou, Cai Jilun from Zhenjiang, Gu Suming from Zhejiang, Ran Xizhang from Nanjing, Ying Xiansan from Shanghai, Cheng Shuli from Suzhou, Zhang Shanqing from Wuxi, Su Laifan from Changshu, Lang Jinpu from Nantong, Zhuge Shenfu from Dongtai, Ying Qianzu from Banpu, Zhu Zhixun from Anhui, Tian Qishan from Wuxing, She Wenkang and Zhang Boxun from Jiangxi. Representatives from other provinces and cities, including Henan, Hebei, Hubei, Hunan, Shandong, Fujian, Sichuan, Tianjin, Beiping, and Qingdao, would be nominated after small group meetings and then report to the guild hall.

Principles Approved

The Shanghai Gold and Silver Industry Guild's opinions on the Ministry's silver product silver usage management regulations were presented at the national assembly for discussion and then approved as follows: Article 2 (original omitted) cannot be accepted by the industry. Although three requests for revision were submitted, all were rejected and we must fight to the death. Article 3 (original omitted) The gold and silver stores that are members of this guild have never sold raw silver ingots, and have repeatedly stated this, so there is no need for discussion. Article 4 (original omitted) The reporting procedures have been approved for the first time and will be handled according to the approval. Article 5 (original omitted) In addition to selling and buying silver materials according to regulations, the number of insufficient materials will be purchased from the Central Bank of China with pure silver, which will be melted and guaranteed. The same joint responsibility will be accepted. Article 6 (original omitted) contradicts Article 2. Since Article 2 cannot be complied with, there is no need to set a standard of 30%. Free business is still required. Article 7 (original omitted) Comply with the order to report the quantity sold every six months to the industry association, which will forward it to the Chamber of Commerce, which will forward it to the local Central Bank or Bank of Communications for verification. Article 8 (original omitted) If a gold and silver shop that is a member of this guild encounters a business closure, the remaining silver ornaments and raw materials will be purchased by the members, reported to the guild, and then forwarded to the Chamber of Commerce and the Central Bank for filing to avoid the abandonment of decoration labor costs. Article 9 (original omitted) In the event of theft or attempted theft, the same responsibility will be taken in accordance with the Article 5 guarantee. There will be no irregular actions. If the above occurs, it will naturally be handled according to law. Article 10 (original omitted) Strictly follow the principles, but the inspection authorities should first order the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and this association to send personnel to handle it together to avoid misunderstandings. Article 11 (original omitted) Request that the Ministry of Finance recognize the gold and silver industry as a special handicraft art, and check and follow previous requests to approve the filing of the following note so that it will not be subject to the 30% restriction of Articles 2 and 6. Two principles of petitioning: 1. Pure silver should still be used for silver jewelry. 2. Eight-part silver (i.e., eight parts silver and two parts copper) may be used for utensils and gifts. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Telegrams Sent Nationwide

Yesterday, the association sent special telegrams to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and various ministries and departments, as well as national organizations, stating: "We, the gold and silver industry of the whole country, upon receiving the silver usage management promulgated by the Ministry of Finance in November of this year, which limits the use of chemical silver to manufacture utensils and ornaments, and only allows the mixing of 30% pure silver when necessary, deeply understand that chemical silver is hard and brittle, making it difficult to manufacture by hand. This will cause hundreds of thousands of workers across the country to fall into unemployment. We have repeatedly requested to revise the regulations and eliminate restrictions, but unfortunately, we have not been approved. On the 23rd of this month, we gathered in Shanghai and convened a joint assembly of the gold and silver industry of the whole country at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Over 600 representatives registered and jointly decided to organize a petition group to make earnest appeals to the authorities. We hereby send a special telegram requesting your inspection and compassion (granting assistance) to achieve the purpose of revision and maintain the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of workers across the country. The telegram is extremely urgent and sincere."

Memorial to the Ministry of Finance

Memorial regarding earnestly requesting revision of the silver usage management regulations, eliminating restrictions on silver content, to maintain the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of silver workers across the country, and to implement the Prime Minister's Principle of People's Livelihood. We, the merchants, previously received the Ministry's silver product silver usage management regulations, which limited the use of chemical silver to manufacture utensils, and only allowed the use of 30% pure silver when necessary. Upon learning of this, everyone was alarmed and at a loss. They all believed that chemical silver is beneficial for machine manufacturing and cannot be competed with by handicrafts. Even with the use of 30% pure silver, it is still hard and brittle and cannot withstand hammering. Therefore, colleagues from various provinces have submitted memorials one after another requesting to revise the regulations, eliminate restrictions on silver content, and divide the reporting of silver inventory into two types: silver utensils and silver materials, for simplicity. We have recently received your approval to divide the reporting of silver inventory into two types, and permission has been granted. However, the silver usage issue has not been allowed to be changed in the slightest. We, humble commoners, dare not have any different opinions on this brilliant decree. However, considering the livelihood of silver workers across the country, it is really impossible to bow our heads and wait for death. Furthermore, it has a great relationship with national essence and customs, so we dare to risk offense and present our case to the Ministry again. As for the fact that chemical silver is hard and brittle, it has already been thoroughly understood by the Ministry. Therefore, in the instructions, there is guidance that "but after heating and hammering, it should not encounter difficulties." We are deeply grateful for your concern and guidance for industry and commerce. However, even if heating and hammering can barely create utensils, they will certainly not be exquisite and beautiful and will eventually be rejected by society. We, the merchants and colleagues, have always used pure silver to manufacture jewelry. However, eight-part silver is used to make utensils. However, it is already difficult during work. The reason for doing so is to make the material slightly stronger and less prone to collision, so as to resist imported silverware. It was never a pleasure to do so. Now, if we are forced to use chemical silver and restrict silver content, then silversmiths will have difficulty applying their skills. I am afraid that foreigners who use machines will take this opportunity to compete with machine-made products and flood in, taking the place of our thousands of years of craftsmanship and causing silversmiths across the country to be eliminated. In recent years, the number of unemployed people in the country has increased day by day. Cries of hunger and cold have followed one another. Some have taken risks out of desperation, and others have been forced to commit suicide. Examining the reasons for their unemployment, the prosperity of machinery and the obsolescence of handicrafts are the primary causes. Now, there are no less than hundreds of thousands of silversmiths across the country. Once they are eliminated, hundreds of thousands of more unemployed people will be added to society. I think that the late Prime Minister always valued the people's livelihood. Now the government wants to implement good policies, but it hinders the people's livelihood. Is this not focusing on one thing and losing sight of the other? We believe that the Ministry's intention in cracking down on silver products is only to prevent the leakage of silver. However, the silver industry in the provinces has explained in detail that silver utensils and ornaments will certainly not be leaked. If you are concerned that colleagues among us may secretly sell silver materials that have not been made into utensils, thus leaking out, then we are willing to provide joint and several guarantees. Strict customs inspections are sufficient to stop smuggling. Why should we give up eating because of choking, and simply cut off the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of people? Our country values gold and silver and despises copper, iron, tin, and lead. It has been like this for thousands of years. The reason why gold and silver are valuable and copper, iron, tin, and lead are cheap is that gold and silver are resistant to water and fire, without any consumption or erosion, and can always maintain their value, while copper, iron, tin, and lead have the danger of rusting. Moreover, when people have abundant wealth, purchasing silverware is no different from saving. Common people often waste pocket money. If they put it into utensils, they will not be willing to give it up easily unless it is absolutely necessary. Therefore, although gold and silver utensils seem luxurious, they can actually cultivate thrift. Moreover, because of their valuable value, they can be used to alleviate emergencies. If chemical silver is easily rusted, it cannot always maintain its value. Once made into utensils, they will be like scrap copper and rotten iron and will not be sufficient to store for emergencies. Furthermore, the aesthetic concept of the Chinese people cannot be completely eliminated. Because its value is not very expensive, there is a rush to compete for novelty and beauty, with endless patterns. It is purchased today and discarded tomorrow. Now the government is training the people to be frugal, but it is starting a trend of extravagance, so how can the people save? The reason why our country is inferior to other countries is machinery. The reason why other countries are inferior to our country is handicrafts. Therefore, our country's old crafts have long been valued by other countries. The carving of silversmiths has the same cultural and artistic skills as bamboo engraving and stone carving. It can also be called a national essence. Now the government wants to promote cultural arts and preserve the national essence, but it restricts silversmiths, preventing them from developing their skills, simply giving foreigners the opportunity to invade with machinery and cutting off the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of people. This is not only self-abandonment, but also a violation of the Prime Minister's principle of giving priority to the people's livelihood. In short, no matter what, there is no risk of silver products leaking out. There is no difference between silver in the hands of the people and in the hands of the government. The gold and silver industry has long been lifeless today. We know that the survival of an industry is not important to the government. Even if we cry out and call for help, it is not enough to move the compassion of those above. However, we must be clear and dare to state our case because we are petitioning for the lives of hundreds of thousands of silversmiths. If they are reduced to unemployment, where will the Ministry place them? Therefore, we are forced to submit this memorial together, earnestly requesting your compassion and approval to revise the silver usage management regulations, eliminating restrictions on the content of silver, so as to implement the Prime Minister's Principle of People's Livelihood and maintain the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of silver workers. Birds about to die cry mournfully. We ask that you have compassion, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance.

Yesterday, the association sent special letters in the name of the assembly to Shanghai business leaders Yu Zhiqing, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, and Lin Kanghou, requesting assistance. The original letter stated: "Respected gentlemen Qiaqing, Yuesheng, Zuoting, and Kanghou, unfortunately, in recent years, our industry has been affected by the weakness of the social economy and the prevalence of women cutting their hair. The decline in our business has been like an autumn forest after frost, with only dead branches remaining. Therefore, those who cannot support themselves and go bankrupt are following one another. The rest are simply trying to maintain the livelihood of their employees and maintain the facade. We only hope that we will not be pruned in the future, or we may be able to survive for a few more years. Who knew that misfortune would come and disaster would occur unexpectedly. On November 4th of last year, the Ministry of Finance promulgated silver product silver usage management regulations, which do not allow the manufacture of utensils and ornaments with pure silver and force the use of chemical silver made of zinc, copper, and lead. Only 30% pure silver is allowed to be mixed in when necessary. This is no different from putting us in a desperate situation and driving all employees to the path of unemployment. Therefore, colleagues from various provinces were alarmed and submitted petitions to the Ministry of Finance one after another to revise the regulations and eliminate restrictions, but unfortunately, they have not been approved. We believe that our industry has always occupied a considerable position in commerce, and its relationship to the prosperity of the market is not insignificant, especially in Shanghai. Now, pure silver is prohibited and replaced with chemical silver. Regardless of whether it is hard and brittle or difficult to manufacture by hand, it will certainly not be able to meet the psychological needs of society. The demise of our industry can be counted on the fingers. To revive commerce and prosper the market is something that the government attaches importance to. However, chemical silver hinders the lifeline of our industry. Has the authorities not considered this yet? Therefore, we and others have no choice but to consider petitioning the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to make earnest requests. We are afraid that our voices are too weak to be heard. We hope that you, gentlemen, have high moral character and are respected by the authorities. You have always protected merchants in every possible way. Therefore, we earnestly ask you to come forward and preside over the matter, lend a hand, and explain our predicament to the authorities in detail. Please add strength and let the opinions from below reach the ears of those above. We believe that the authorities will give credence to and show compassion to your earnest words, and will change their minds and allow our industry to survive. Then all the hundreds of thousands of employees across the country will be grateful forever. We are attaching the original draft of the petition memorial for your reference and assistance."

Closed Yesterday

The gold and silver industry in this city is divided into two types: old firms and new firms. Old firms are gold and silver stores with a long history and large scale, totaling 14. New firms are smaller, totaling 16, and there are 120 other related businesses. Therefore, there are a total of more than 150 gold and silver stores in the city. Yesterday was the date of the national gold and silver industry representative assembly, so it was specially closed for one day. All large gold and silver stores were closed, but a few other businesses remained open as usual.

Jianghai Customs Yesterday Published January Data: City's Imports and Exports - Increased Exports, Drastically Reduced Imports - A Positive Sign for Foreign Trade 84

According to Shen Shi News Agency, yesterday, the Customs released the foreign trade data for this city in January. Exports increased, imports decreased, resulting in a trade surplus, the second time since the establishment of the Customs itself (the first time was in December last year). The total value of imports and exports for this city in January is recorded below:

French Concession Telephone Users Issue Declaration Yesterday - Will Disconnect Services if Demands Are Not Met 86

Huang Xianggu, Mao Yun, Jin Liren, Cai Hongtian, Shang Mujiang, Gong Jingyan, Lu Zhizheng, Zhang Shishi, Zai Manyun, Lin Kecong, Zhu Xuefan, Zhang Yingzeng, Lü Qiuren, Xia Weiqing, Xu Wenrong, Xu Keren, Xu Zhenyu, Huang Zhaoxiong, He Yuanming, Du Gang, Wu Xiu, Qu Zhenhua, Gu Wensheng, Tang Huimin, Zhu Wende, Chen Kecheng, and other 1,647 telephone users in the French Concession, issued a declaration yesterday in opposition to the new telephone fee regulations: "The Shanghai Telephone Company, disregarding public opinion, will implement new regulations from March 1st, effectively increasing prices in disguise. The Public Concession's Municipal Council is also maintaining its so-called one percent official profit and resolutely approving the regulations, without first seeking the consent of the French Concession's Board of Directors. The Public Concession's Municipal Council has no opportunity to consider the company's new fee regulations. Although the Chinese directors attending the French Concession's Board of Directors have made efforts to hold differing opinions, they ultimately cannot achieve the fundamental purpose of our decision. As a compromise, the duration of each call, a generally unspoken issue, has been extended from the strict limitation of three minutes to five minutes. Although this matter is minor, according to the company's statistics, it will also result in significant losses. Regarding the two proposals to increase the number of calls and reduce the base fee, there has been no way to raise them. It is rumored that if the French Concession's Board of Directors' initial proposal is followed, increasing the number of calls from 100 to 150 for residential users and from 150 to 200 for commercial users, the company would lose 40,000 yuan per month. However, the company's expenses can certainly be reduced by more than this 40,000 yuan. Since this arbitration proposal, which is beneficial to the company, cannot be accepted, it is clear that the French Concession's Board of Directors can no longer make proposals. Therefore, the company's new regulations, scheduled to be implemented on March 1st, have become an unshakeable iron law. The company's desire to increase prices has been long-standing. As far back as July of the 21st year of the Republic of China, the original price rate was increased by 25 percent, with residential users increasing from 52 taels of silver to 65 taels, and commercial users increasing from 78 taels of silver to 105 taels. Fifteen months later, in October of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, there was another proposal to increase prices by one-fifth. Although this was not realized, its insatiable desire for extortion was fully exposed. Is this the proper attitude of an enterprise? Is this the means that a public utility should have? Although telephone users have strongly resisted each time, they are scattered like sand and ultimately suppressed. This has happened more than once in history. The company is accustomed to this situation and will do as it pleases, violating laws and reason. It will increase prices three times in as many years, and users will be helpless. We, the telephone users, looking to the future, must unite to resist the company's tyranny and eradicate future oppression. We are willing to endure the pain now. If the demands put forward by the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession cannot be met, we will disconnect our services. We know that the company cannot be reasoned with, so we will use passive resistance to issue a serious warning, hoping to prevent endless exploitation in the future. This is our declaration. February 23rd, 25th year of the Republic of China."

Shortage of 20-Cent Nickel Auxiliary Coins - Additional 240,000 Yuan Minted - Mint Has Delivered to Central Bank 87

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the Central Mint, due to the shortage of 20-cent nickel coins after the issuance of the new auxiliary coins, has recently increased the minting of 240,000 yuan to meet the demand. These coins have been delivered to the Central Bank for exchange and circulation. At the same time, a strict investigation is being conducted to identify and crack down on counterfeiters of the new auxiliary coins. Details are as follows:

Increased Minting of Nickel Coins

Since the official issuance of the new auxiliary coins on the tenth of this month, the demand for exchange has increased sharply in various places, resulting in an insufficient distribution of the original three types of nickel coins and two types of copper coins. Among them, the 20-cent nickel coins were the most scarce, as the original blanks were all imported from abroad. The first batch that arrived in Shanghai was small in quantity, so it was sold out within a few days of issuance. It is now reported that the second batch of 20-cent nickel blanks has arrived and is being mass-minted by the Central Mint, with patterns engraved. A total of 240,000 yuan has been minted, packed into 80 large boxes, each containing 15,000 coins, worth 3,000 yuan. They were successively transported to the Central Bank in the past two days for distribution and exchange in various places, which should temporarily alleviate the shortage.

Strict Investigation of Counterfeiting

The Central Mint, upon the order of the Ministry of Finance, is investigating the discovery of counterfeit new auxiliary coins in the market shortly after their issuance. If confirmed, strict measures should be taken. After receiving the order, the mint has already begun a strict investigation to crack down on counterfeiters. According to the person in charge of the mint, rumors of counterfeit new auxiliary coins have been circulating for several days. Although the actual situation is unknown, since a small number have already been discovered in the market, prompt action should be taken to prevent future problems. Although nickel coins are hard and difficult to mint, since the original blanks are imported from abroad, if they fall into the hands of counterfeiters, they only need to add a pattern, and there will be an opportunity for counterfeiting. However, the patterns of counterfeit coins are mostly poor and blurry, which is easy to distinguish compared to the fine and clear patterns of genuine coins.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Employee Screening - Written Examination Held Yesterday - All Examination Committee Members Arrived at the Bureau - Results Awaiting Judgment and Submission to the Ministry for Announcement 89

According to Central News Agency, the employee screening examination for the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was held yesterday morning. All members of the Examination Committee attended the bureau to administer the examination, which lasted until noon. The examination papers will be judged by the Examination Committee, and the results will be announced within a few days. The details of the examination are recorded below:

Announcement of Measures

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is implementing restructuring, revising the organizational law, and saving expenses. It has specifically stipulated the number of employees in each department and section. However, since the original number of employees exceeded the stipulated number, the ministry announced employee screening examination measures and appointed members of the Examination Committee to be followed by the bureau. An oral examination was conducted earlier, with Chairman Committee member Lu Hanqin, appointed by the ministry, together with other committee members, separately summoning the bureau's employees for individual oral examinations.

Written Examination Held

The written examination was held yesterday. All employees of the bureau gathered at the bureau before 9:00 a.m. Examination Committee members Lu Hanqin, Lu Rongguang, Peng Hu, Wei Yifu, Ma Xun, Hu Jizhong, Lu Shaoxian, Hu Renyuan, and others also arrived at the bureau to administer the examination. The employees gathered in their respective departments and sat down in their original seats. The examination papers and questions were then distributed by the Examination Committee. The examination ended at around 12:00 noon.

Different Examination Questions

The written examination questions differed according to the work of each employee. In addition to the two subjects of Chinese language and Party doctrine, technical personnel had questions related to navigation administration and docks, while accounting personnel had questions related to finance and accounting. Ordinary employees and staff members were tested on official documents and calligraphy. The examination papers will be judged by the Examination Committee and then submitted to the ministry for review and announcement, to determine who will be retained and who will be dismissed.

Ministry of Finance Amends Insurance Stamp Tax Law - Exempting Those with Insurance Amounts Less Than 1,000 Yuan 94

Guomin News Agency: The Ministry of Finance has amended the Stamp Tax Law. For insurance policies issued by insurance companies: For personal insurance, a stamp tax of 2 cents will be levied for every 1,000 yuan of the insured amount, and any amount exceeding 1,000 yuan will also be calculated as 1,000 yuan. For property insurance, a stamp tax of 1 cent will be levied for every 1,000 yuan of the insured amount, and any amount exceeding 1,000 yuan will also be calculated as 1,000 yuan. However, the maximum stamp tax for each item is limited to 3 yuan, and the responsibility lies with the person who establishes the evidence. All items with an insured amount of less than 1,000 yuan are exempt from stamp tax. Insurance businesses run by the government and insurance policies issued for labor insurance businesses are exempt from stamp tax. This tax rate has been announced and implemented. It is reported that the Chamber of Commerce in this city will also notify various insurance companies to comply with the regulations.

British and French Concessions - Work Together to Prevent Opium - Dispatch Personnel Every Night to Investigate Hotels and Opium Dens - Gradually Eliminate Opium Dens in Lanes and Alleys, and Clearance Is Expected 95

Huadong News Agency: Since the city authorities organized the Anti-Opium Committee, opium addicts have been enthusiastically registering, and those who are quitting are constantly on the way. In order to thoroughly eliminate opium in Shanghai, the Anti-Opium Committee has joined forces with the British and French Concessions to jointly prohibit opium. It is now learned that the two Concessions have been very cooperative recently in preventing opium. They also dispatch personnel every night to conduct investigations, so as to avoid the existence of secret opium dens in hotels and alleys. The details are recorded as follows:

During the Early Prohibition Period, Opium Addicts Avoided

Since the city organized the Anti-Opium Committee this year, those who obeyed the order to register were very enthusiastic. However, stubborn opium addicts still followed the old ways and avoided the authorities. This city has always been a city where Chinese and foreigners live together, and the Concession areas have become a refuge for opium addicts. Not only do opium addicts from this city gather in the Concessions, but also those from other ports come to Shanghai from afar to hide there.

Concession Authorities Cooperate to Prevent Opium

After the Anti-Opium Committee and the municipal authorities requested the British and French Concessions to jointly prohibit opium, the Concessions provided assistance. Therefore, opium dens in the Concessions have recently disappeared. However, according to confidential reports, there have been opium addicts who have rented rooms and opened opium dens to provide opium for addicts hiding in the Concessions to smoke.

Dispatch Personnel Every Night to Investigate Hotels

The two authorities, after receiving the reports, dispatch personnel every night to investigate the whereabouts of travelers and urge the hotel authorities to be strict to see if there are any shelter situations. Once discovered, they will be punished according to the law. Therefore, opium has completely disappeared from hotels.

Opium Dens in Lanes and Alleys Expected to Be Cleared

The investigation of opium dens in the common lanes is also very strict. The opium addicts call it "martial law." All petty criminals also lack the ability to cheat. It is heard that, when necessary, they will check every household as the municipal authorities do, so the clearance of opium in the Concessions can be expected.

National Representatives of the Western Medicine Association Petition in Beijing: The Nation's Difficulties are Severe, the Physician's Duty is Important: Petition Resulted in Satisfaction, Recruiting Members 102

The Chinese Western Medicine Association convened its Third National Representative Congress a month ago. Considering that our country has a vast territory and a large population, and the number of Western doctors is insufficient, the congress resolved to send Qian Longzhang, Ye Qubo, Zhang Kelun, Ni Genghua, Liu Xinbo, Yao Zuodun, Zhang Guowei, Huang Aihua, Zeng Xianzhong, Cai Damin, Chu Zhemin, Chu Wenhui, Lu Xiaolin, Gong Yan, Qu Shichang, Liu Renfu, and overseas representative Yang Zhaoji, secretary Qiu Pingsan, and more than forty representatives from various provinces, cities, and counties to Beijing on February 2nd to petition. Now, it is reported that the representatives have completed their mission and returned to their respective hometowns. The representatives gathered in Shanghai and returned to Shanghai from Beijing. The details are recorded as follows:

Petition Process

After the representatives arrived in Beijing, they first respectfully went to the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum to pay their respects. Then, they went to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Health to petition. Secretary-General Weng, Director Liu, and Director Zhou separately received them. Before the promulgation of the Western Medicine Regulations in the 18th year of the Republic (1929), those who have the flexibility to practice medicine will be issued a medical practice license, and the license period will be set for half a year. Those who practiced medicine in the 18th year of the Republic (and have six years of experience so far) will be issued a three-year assistant doctor license, and a medical practice certificate will be exchanged after the expiration. The government understood the people’s concerns and considered public opinion to be reasonable. It has been planning and approving the notification.

Representatives' Feelings

According to Chief Representative Qian Longzhang and Secretary Qiu Pingsan, they were very happy to be able to visit the capital during this petition and felt that our country's politics is on track, and the government's concern for the people's hardships and the following of public opinion fully demonstrates the spirit of democracy. In particular, Director Liu of the Ministry of Health and Director Zhou of the Medical Administration Department are more familiar with social conditions and care for the people's livelihood. At this time when the world situation is dangerous and our country is in serious trouble, we should strengthen unity to support the government, and the doctor's duty is especially important in relation to public health and national health. When the country is in trouble, military doctors serve, which is more important than any other group. Therefore, the meeting has concentrated on gathering medical talents from all over the country and expanding the recruitment of members to enrich the strength and serve the people. It is hoped that the public opinion will give assistance to achieve satisfactory results.

Cai Xianzong, a local resident, 38 years old, has been running a butcher shop in Lan Nidu, Pudong. Cai has an ugly face, but is quite honest. He learned that the woman's name was Wu Qiaozhen, 23 years old, from Nanhui, and had been engaged in prostitution for a long time. Cai staggered back, quite remorseful. Not only that, the hotel tea room waiter and Qiaozhen saw that Cai was weak and could be deceived, and introduced a Ningbo man named Ling Aliang, who claimed to be Qiaozhen's husband, to scare Cai. On this self-proclaimed Qiaozhen's husband of Ningbo, Qiaozhen led by another man named Pei Tingbao, and brought more than 20 fierce women to Cai's shop to make trouble, claiming that Qiaozhen was Ling's third concubine, and that he had been raped and defiled, and that the jade bracelet and two gold rings she was wearing had been cheated away, a total of more than 500 yuan. Cai was forced to compensate. The quarrel lasted until 2:00 AM, and Cai's friends persuaded them to leave. Those who came asked Cai to reason in the teahouse, but they failed. On the day before, they took the initiative to compromise in Cai's shop, reducing the amount from 500 yuan to 50 yuan, which could be settled. Otherwise, they would force Qiaozhen to commit suicide in Cai's shop as a threat. Cai, who had been infected with syphilis, had a rotten lower body and suffered without recourse. He still wanted to set up words to frighten him to pay money, so he submitted a report to the Pudong Sub-Bureau yesterday for investigation at any time. Chu Minggao, a native of Tiantai, Zhejiang, worked in the Shaanxi Provincial Department of Education. In the 20th year of the Republic (1931), he lived with his wife Jin Yueqin in Zhabei. Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, when Zhabei was on the front line, Chu and his wife fled to the concession. At that time, Jin Yueqin was pregnant and due. On the fourteenth day of the first lunar month of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), she gave birth to a son, and Chu left without saying goodbye. Jin Yueqin lost her dependence and was extremely miserable. Recently, Yu Yueqin went to Changzhou and met her husband Chu Minggao on the train, and saw that her husband was accompanied by a young woman. She could not help but be angry and asked him for money, but Chu accused Jin Yueqin of running away from her husband and committing adultery with someone, and they mutually arrested at the North Station Police Bureau. Chu insisted that the clothing store owner Huang Chanlin had an affair with Jin Yueqin, and Jin Daodao Qin Yi found out that her husband had remarried with a woman named Xu Jingfang, and was ordered to be transferred to the local court for nuclear verification, while Yu Youyou declared in the newspaper that Jin Yueqin had misconduct with Huang, and Huang Chanlin was aggrieved for being insulted for no reason, so he hired a lawyer to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Court of the Local Court, accusing Chu Minggao of defaming him and other circumstances. Huang was 42 years old, from Changzhou, and opened a clothing store. Jin Yueqin was a servant in my house, but Chu Minggao falsely accused me of being an adulterer, and then destroyed my reputation by publishing in the newspaper. He requested legal action. Then, according to Jin Yueqin's testimony, she was 27 years old, from Suzhou, and married Chu Minggao on March 28th of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), renting a house in Zhabei. Later, he abandoned me without news due to the war, and remarried with a woman named Xu Jingfang, and falsely accused me of committing adultery with Huang Chanlin. He was really heartless. He asked for an investigation. The judge obtained the testimony and ordered Chu Minggao, who was in custody, to be brought to the case (Chu was in custody for remarriage). He testified that he was 29 years old and worked in the education field. Jin Yueqin ran away without a trace during the refuge, so he remarried Xu Jingfang on January 22nd of this year. The next day, he met his runaway wife on the way back to Shanghai from Nanjing, and called the police to arrest her. He also admitted that he published a statement in the newspaper on February 4th, etc. Lawyer Dong stated that the dissemination of text was related to private morals, and the defendant was guilty of harming the private prosecutor's reputation and deserved punishment. He requested that a judgment be made in accordance with the law. The judge believed that the case was clear and considered it to be concluded. The verdict was announced yesterday that Chu Minggao disseminated text and damaged the reputation of others, and was fined 50 yuan. If he was to be sentenced to labor service, one yuan would be converted into one day, suspended for five years. After the verdict, he was returned to custody pending further instructions.

Chinese Ancient Coin Society Established Yesterday 113

The Chinese Ancient Coin Society, initiated by ancient coin experts at home and abroad, has been prepared and was officially established at Gongdelin yesterday (23rd) afternoon. Attendees included Wu Zhihui, Zhang Shuxun, Ye Yufu, Ding Zhong, Yang Kailing, Wei Juxian, Jian Youwen, Cheng Yuncen, Zheng Shixu, Yu Daxiong, Zong Libai, and dozens of others. The meeting was grand and lively. After the temporary chairman Ding Fubao held the founding ceremony, the constitution was passed, and Ding Fubao was elected as the chairman, Ye Yufu and Zhang Shuxun as the vice-chairmen, and Fang Yaoyu, Zhang Gangbo, Xuan Guyu, Zheng Jiaxiang, Deng Qiumei, Cheng Wuquan, Wei Juxian, Zhang Jijing, and Cao Hengzhi as the councilors, Wu Zhihui, Jian Youwen, Yu Daxiong, Zheng Shixu, Zong Libai, and Yang Kailing as the directors. After the ceremony, a group photo was taken and it was already 6:00 PM. The bylaws of the association are recorded as follows: This association is named the Chinese Ancient Coin Society. The purpose of this association is to clarify ancient coin knowledge, study the production of ancient coins, identify authenticity, distinguish eras, and inspire people's interests. All those who are interested in ancient coins can apply to join the association. After being introduced by a member, filling out a volunteer form, and passing the Shanghai Council, they will become members of this association. Foreign comrades can become honorary members of this association after the procedures of the previous article. The funds of this association are from voluntary donations from members. After being approved by the Council and the Board of Directors, membership fees may be charged. Each member pays at least two yuan in national currency per year. This association has one president, two vice-presidents, nine councilors, and five directors. They are elected or nominated by the general meeting of members of each term and can be re-elected. This association may be recommended by the Board of Directors to have one to two honorary presidents, who will be invited to take office by the chairman. This association holds a general meeting once a year, convened by the chairman, and a research meeting once a month. In addition to discussing association affairs and exchanging knowledge, members may bring their collections or writings for mutual appreciation. The Council and the Board of Directors are convened by the chairman when necessary. This association may issue various publications to publicize to fellows, which will be planned and handled by the Council and the Board of Directors. This association is located in Shanghai and may establish branches in various places. If there are any outstanding matters in these bylaws, they can be revised by the General Assembly. It is also heard that the association's communication address has been set at Medical Book Bureau, Ding Fubao, Maibaike Road, and Yang Kailing, Central Bank.

Health Department of the Public Works Bureau Announces the Source and Prevention of Smallpox 114

Spring Vaccination Work in the Chinese Concession to Begin Soon. The spring vaccination work in the city will be started by both the Municipal Health Bureau and the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession. According to the announcement by the Health Department of the Public Works Bureau regarding the source and prevention of smallpox, smallpox is one of the most widespread and terrifying infectious diseases in China. It is a type of tiny germ, the shape of which is so small that even with the most powerful microscope, it cannot be observed. However, through various experiments, we know how it invades the human body and have a truly effective method of prevention. Current vaccination procedures are extremely simple. If proper attention is paid during implementation, those being vaccinated will experience very little discomfort. It is commonly believed that infants suffer during vaccination, but this is not the case. Infants and young children are more susceptible to smallpox than adults, so vaccination should be given special attention. Caution, cleanliness, and isolation can reduce the spread of smallpox, but vaccination can completely prevent it.

Xing Zhigang, a representative of the shipping industry in Pudong West, submitted a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday requesting an investigation and prohibition of disturbances at harbors. The petition stated: "Regarding the false pretense of names and the extortion of levies, it is requested that the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau be ordered to strictly prohibit and maintain the safety of shipping and travel. The Nanhuiguan Wharf and the Gongyi Public Wharf in Nanshi are busy areas for the berthing of ships from Pudong West. Recently, idlers outside the industry have been falsely using the name of the civilian shipping industry to threaten rural ships at the Nanhuiguan and Gongyi Public Wharves, extorting air transport donations of one yuan, six dimes, or three dimes per month per ship, lingering at the harbors, and arbitrarily harassing them, causing unbearable suffering. The Public Security Bureau has previously investigated and prohibited this. Now the harassment continues as before. We would be deeply grateful."

Overview of Public Concession Police Personnel Work in the Past Year, Three Chinese Detectives and Chinese Constables Establish Special Merits, Fierce Battle with Robbers Results in Loss of One Policeman 116

The Public Works Bureau Intelligence Office released the Public Concession Police Department's 1935 annual report, which was previously submitted to the Public Works Bureau Board of Directors. The key points are excerpted and disclosed below.

Police Chief Major General Jardine took leave to return to his country in early April of that year. From April 7th to December 31st, the Chief's duties were temporarily assumed by Deputy Chief Major General Bourne.

In that year, the police personnel who received awards for special merits included Chinese Detective Jin Wanrong, who was loyal and brave during the war against heinous bandits and was awarded the first-class medal for special merits. Chinese Constable Wu Zonghai also demonstrated both wisdom and courage while capturing bandits and was awarded the second-class medal for special merits. Furthermore, Chinese Detective Zhang Jinlong, number 90, died from injuries sustained while pursuing bandits. His loyalty, bravery, and decisiveness are truly admirable, and he was posthumously awarded the second-class medal for distinguished service. Statistics for that year show that police personnel engaged in fierce battles with bandits a total of eighteen times. The police suffered one death and six injuries, while twelve bandits were killed and injured. Regarding the patrol constables, as of the end of the year, the number of Chinese constables and patrolmen under the jurisdiction of the Police Department was 3,791, Russian constables were 100, and Indian constables were 380. All of these numbers showed slight decreases compared to the previous year.

There were no difficulties encountered in recruiting qualified personnel for various positions that year, and the general level of new recruits was adequately maintained. A total of 82 new constables were recruited this year, all of whom were trained and dispatched to serve. The Westerners who joined the police force were all recruited locally. Regarding discipline, with the exception of those whose circumstances were serious and who had received appropriate punishment, all personnel were able to abide by the rules and were deemed satisfactory. The health of police personnel was excellent this year. The average daily percentage of sick police officers was 3.41% for Western constables, 5.30% for Japanese constables, 2.77% for Indian constables, and only 1.78% for Chinese constables.

The Central Police Station and the Police Department began operations on June 3rd of that year. Now all the central police offices are concentrated in one place, which is a major reform in terms of work efficiency. This year, the Police Department armory repaired a total of 5,899 firearms, and no unusable firearms were found throughout the year. One new bulletproof vest was added this year, bringing the total to 354, as well as 80 steel shields. Furthermore, 126 new constables and 133 patrol constables underwent shooting practice with large and small pistols or Mauser pistols, using more than 150,000 rounds of ammunition in total. The shooting skills of each police officer were excellent. This year, the reserve police force was dispatched to suppress riots and robberies a total of 13 times, most of which were not of great importance and had no use for force when they arrived on the scene. They were able to perform their other routine duties, such as assisting police officers in checking pedestrians and guarding the courts, satisfactorily.

This year, the mounted patrol team had a total of eight large horses and thirty-nine small horses. Five small horses were euthanized due to old age. At the end of this year, the Public Concession had a total of 485 special agents, with 73 newly enlisted and 67 retired. There were three shooting competitions. They assisted ordinary police personnel in their duties, including household surveys, the abolished lunar New Year, and the 50th anniversary of the British Emperor's coronation. These agents were extremely efficient, and three of them have received long service medals.

Executive Committee Meeting. Chen Mingjian was elected as chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the minutes. The meeting was convened as scheduled. The proposed motions are recorded below. The chairman reported on the resolutions of the previous meeting. The Qingdao Association stated that it would resign from its position as a standing committee member. It was resolved that standing committee members who cannot attend due to unforeseen circumstances should delegate representatives from other associations to attend. Resolved: Standing committee members who cannot attend due to unforeseen circumstances may delegate executive committee representatives. The Changsha Association proposed, and the Hankou Association seconded, that the proposal of the Executive Committee regarding the Cangwu Association should be reconsidered. It was resolved to pass. The Shanghai Association proposed, and the Tongshan Association seconded, that the rules of procedure for Article 12 of the Articles of Association and the rules of procedure for Article 22 be drafted by the standing committee. It was resolved to pass. The Jinhua Association proposed that executive committee and standing committee members who cannot attend the meeting should delegate other executive committee representatives to attend the meeting, and if they fail to do so for three consecutive meetings without delegating a representative, they should be replaced by a majority of the committee members. Resolved: Passed. Secretary-General Liu Liumin proposed, in accordance with Article 8 of the Articles of Association, that Liu Zuwang, Dai Tianqiu, Yan Yinwu, Yu Naiduo, Cai Li, Zhang Shijie, Chen Yao, Gong Shengzhi, Hu Jiaxin, and other nine people be appointed as secretaries. It was resolved to pass. Secretary-General Liu Liumin proposed to inquire about the internal and external powers and responsibilities. Resolved: The external documents of the Association should be jointly signed and held responsible by the standing committee and the secretary-general. Internal documents should be signed and held responsible by the secretary-general personally. This power should be stipulated in the rules of procedure. The Jing City Association reported that the resolutions of the General Assembly, except for those that should be handled by the General Assembly, should be taken over by the Association. Resolved: Passed. It should be accepted for handling. The Jiangdu Association proposed that a standing committee meeting should be held every month, and the secretaries should be notified to attend. Resolved: Passed. It was proposed to convene a standing committee meeting on the 24th of this month and notify all secretaries to attend. Resolved: Passed. The meeting adjourned at 11 o'clock after all items were discussed.

Shanghai Telephone Company Notifies Users of New Charging Methods 119

February bills are still issued as before, and the monthly fee will be pre-charged. Next month, the new rules will be calculated. The Shanghai Telephone Company's new rules for basic call charges will take effect on March 1st. The company has issued another notice to users explaining the charging methods. The original notice stated: "To all telephone users, regarding the announcement issued by our company on February 1st, stating that the new rules should take effect from March 1st of this year, and specifying the monthly billing dates for each district to pre-charge the monthly fee, and to collect the excess local call charges for the previous month in the next month's bill, please note that your payment date originally starts from the 19th of each month to prepay the 'monthly fee' (all telephone numbers starting with '9' follow this example). As for the excess local calls during that month, they should be calculated up to the 16th of the following month and included in the next month's bill. The February bill for this year will still be issued as before, and the March bill will be calculated according to the new rules, and the accounts that need to be sorted out during the transition period of the new and old regulations from March 1st to 18th will be included. The excess local calls during March (calculated from March 1st to 16th, users who originally paid by call will be calculated separately) and the out-of-area call charges before March 16th will be collected together. Shanghai Telephone Company."

International Theater Hosts Chinese Modern Art Exhibition, From the 27th of this Month to the 10th of Next Month, at 55 Yuanmingyuan Road 121

The International Theater of Arts, organized by Chinese and Western artists in Shanghai, performed "Wang Baochuan" at the Shanghai Grand Theater last year, which was well received by the public. Mrs. Fohs, the general manager of the theater, collected 150 oil and ink paintings created recently by 30 famous artists, including Liu Haisu, Wang Yiting, and Wang Jiyuan, and will hold the Chinese Modern Painting Exhibition at the theater at 55 Yuanmingyuan Road in Shanghai from the 27th of this month to the 10th of March. The opening ceremony will be held at the venue at 4 pm on the 27th, and Mayor Wu will be invited to cut the ribbon. It is also reported that the diplomatic corps stationed in Shanghai from various countries will attend the exhibition. The catalog of exhibits has a preface written by Cai Yuanpei, etc. The preface of Cai is recorded as follows: "The intense aesthetic sense and rich imagination contained in Chinese painting create the most perfect aesthetic model in our ideals. Since the Han Dynasty, Chinese painting has occupied a unique position in the history of world art. The excellence of its works, as evidenced by the surviving ones today, proves this. In the Tang Dynasty, Chinese painting was divided into the Northern and Southern schools, which was a major event in the history of Chinese painting. Li Sixun, the leader of the Northern school, created landscape painting. This style flourished in the Song Dynasty. Wang Wei, the master of the Southern school, was unique and pioneered a new path, abandoning the rigid forms of the past and replacing them with soft and gentle brushstrokes. This style still exists today. Commentators often say that Southern school paintings are favored by general literati, while Northern school paintings are favored by artisans. This statement is somewhat too generalized. Judging from historical facts, the primary condition for both the Northern and Southern schools is Xie He's so-called 'qi yun sheng dong' (spiritual consonance, life-movement). This element of painting is not something that anyone can obtain. It is the product of the artist's own rich learning and experience. Therefore, excellent works of our country's painting all have this characteristic, and this is why our country's painting is superior to other countries. Western researchers of Eastern culture are often fascinated by our country's ancient art and neglect Chinese modern art, and even say that there is no modern art to speak of in our country, which is a very wrong view. Taking painting as an example, for thousands of years, its style has continued without interruption. To this day, its painting style not only remains, but is also carried forward by modern artists. Not only do they have a deep understanding of ancient artists in their own country, but they also have a deep understanding of the works of Western masters. Therefore, with the learning of these modern artists, and engaging in the sorting out and development of our country's inherent art, there should be new and extraordinary views and ideas. This International Theater is organizing a modern Chinese painting exhibition, and its exhibitors are all writers who bear the responsibility of revitalizing modern Chinese art. Among the exhibitors, we want to especially mention Liu Haisu, Wang Yiting, Huang Binhong, and Wang Jiyuan. Liu Haisu has spared no effort in promoting modern art in our country, which is well known, and his own talent is unique. In the past 20 years, he has worked hard and studied extensively, and his achievements are to discard the dross of ancient art, liberate our country's art from the decay and decorate it with a fresh and lively face. Mr. Liu is a revolutionary painter who does not compromise. Professor Lai Luggu of France called him 'the master of the revival of Chinese art,' which is well founded. Mr. Liu has traveled to Europe twice to promote our country's art, and has hosted modern Chinese painting exhibitions in various European countries, so that Westerners are relieved of their modern art. His footsteps have been well-received, and he is a great vitality in our country's art world. Wang Yiting and Huang Binhong are both well-learned scholars and famous figures in the art world, and their works have the magic of perfection. Wang Jiyuan is a writer who is constantly striving for progress. His art has its own unique features. He has held solo exhibitions in Japan and Europe in the past, and has been deeply praised by people in those countries. This International Art Association is organizing the Chinese Book Exhibition, which is enough to represent the cooperation between Chinese and foreign cultures. It is hoped that this spirit of cooperation can be continuously expanded and popularized in other Chinese and foreign relations."

Zheng Yongyu Sues Zheng Bozhao, Case Dismissed 122

Zheng Yongchu, the manager of the Yongtai Stack tobacco shop on Henan Road in the city, sued Yue merchant Zheng Bozhao for breach of trust and embezzlement. After repeated summons by the First Special District Court, the judgment was made yesterday (22nd): "Zheng Bozhao dismissed." The reasons for the judgment are as follows: "If the statute of limitations for prosecution has been completed, a judgment of dismissal shall be issued. This is clearly stipulated in Article 294, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law. In this case, the plaintiff sued for embezzlement and breach of trust. The main points of his lawsuit are: 'My father, Zheng Shiqing, and others set up the Yongtai Stack tobacco shop on Henan Road and appointed the defendant as the manager to contract the British American Tobacco Company's brand of cigarettes (ie, Hongxibao cigarettes). Later, Shuitaizhan was reorganized into Yongtaihe, and the defendant was still the manager. Unexpectedly, he violated his duties and took advantage of the Yongtaihe brand name to embezzle the right to sell the British American Tobacco Company's cigarettes on behalf of Yongtai Stack for 28 years. It was not until last year (ie, 24th year of the Republic) that the old correspondence of the defendant and the contract with the British American Tobacco Company were found, and he filed a lawsuit accordingly, etc.' Questioning the defendant, I believe that Yongtaihe and Yongtai Stack have a partnership relationship. It is claimed that Yongtaihe is an independent business and was established in 1912 (ie, the first year of the Republic). In the same year, it contracted the exclusive right to sell British American Tobacco Company's cigarettes and was specifically certified by Fish White, director of the British American Tobacco Company. The British American Tobacco Company's cigarettes were contracted by Zheng Bozhao without exception. The object of the crime of embezzlement in Xingfa is limited to objects, not including rights. This is extremely clear from the meaning of Article 335 of the same law, which refers to embezzling one's own possession of other people's objects. The plaintiff in this case accused the defendant of embezzling its right to contract cigarettes, which does not conform to the requirements of the crime of embezzlement. In terms of procedure, the plaintiff said that the defendant had embezzled its rights and violated his duties for 28 years. According to the statute of limitations of the old and new criminal laws, its right to sue has long been extinguished. Assuming that the British American Tobacco Company contracted cigarettes in 1912 (which is beneficial to the plaintiff), it has been more than 24 years. Even if the plaintiff only discovered evidence of the crime last year (ie, 24th year of the Republic), it cannot be considered a reason for suspending the statute of limitations. Moreover, the crime of embezzlement and breach of trust is a consummated crime. Since the plaintiff pointed out that the defendant's act of contracting was an act of embezzlement and breach of trust, then when his act of contracting was established, the crime was completed. Although he still receives commissions for contracting cigarettes, this is an extension of the benefits obtained after the crime and is different from the continuous state of the crime. Its statute of limitations should be calculated from the first year of the Republic (the period of contracting cigarettes). The law at the time of the defendant's act was the effective period of the Provisional Criminal Law. Comparing Article 69, paragraph 1, sections 3 and 4 of the Criminal Law with Article 80, paragraph 1, section 2 of the Criminal Law, the statute of limitations of the Criminal Law should be applied. According to that law, the statute of limitations for the right to sue for the crime of embezzlement is seven years, and the statute of limitations for the crime of breach of trust is three years. Compared with the defendant's act, which was completed 24 years ago, the statute of limitations in this case has long been completed. According to the above regulations, a judgment of dismissal should be issued, and the judgment is made as the main text."

The Municipal Public Security Bureau announced yesterday that there were 277 criminal cases in the city during the past week from February 15th to 21st. A total of 555 criminals, male and female, were arrested. They are listed as follows: 16 robbery and strong cases, 16 criminals; 86 theft cases, 111 criminals; 43 injury cases, 88 criminals; 27 abduction cases, 51 criminals; 6 gambling cases, 130 criminals; 15 fraud cases, 23 criminals; 2 communist cases, 5 criminals; 1 homicide case, 4 criminals; 4 fire cases, 4 criminals; 12 counterfeit banknote cases, 15 criminals; 7 violations of police regulations, 16 criminals; and 58 other criminal cases, 92 criminals. A total of 277 cases, 555 criminals. All of the above-mentioned criminals have been preliminarily tried by the Third Section. Except for those with minor cases, who were dealt with in accordance with the Violation of Police Regulations Penalty Law, or who were sentenced to release, totaling 88, the remaining criminals have been sent to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. Honest Service from the Clever Advertising Agency 124

The Clever Advertising Design Agency at No. 29 Edward Road was founded by Pan Yihua, an advertising expert. Mr. Pan was formerly a famous journalist in Shanghai, having served in the film industry for over ten years. Countless Chinese and foreign films and actors owe their fame to his promotional efforts. Mr. Pan is known for his expertise in advertising. While in the film industry, various film production companies and cinemas competed to recruit him. Now, due to the economic downturn in Shanghai, Mr. Pan is willing to serve various industrial and commercial enterprises. He has established the Clever Advertising Design Agency and hired art experts at great expense to handle various artistic advertisements. To fully implement the service tenet, fees are extremely low. Any major industrial and commercial enterprises wishing to engage the agency as a permanent advertising consultant need only pay an annual consulting fee of 100 yuan in national currency. For any promotional advertising matters within the year, if the cost does not exceed 1,000 yuan in national currency, no additional fees will be charged. In addition, an art advertising sample department has been established, specifically for shops that do not frequently publish newspaper advertisements. Matters concerning artistic advertisements, storefront layouts, window displays, merchandise labels, promotional activities, wrapping paper, etc., all require artistic thinking. If stores directly hire people to create samples, the cost is very high. Now, the agency only charges a sample fee of two yuan per store per year. This covers all kinds of art advertising samples, regardless of quantity, without any additional fees. If you wish to have them created after the sample is approved, the price is also very low. Moreover, the originality of the ideas and the pleasing nature of the designs are unmatched in Shanghai. Therefore, businesses with discerning eyes entrust their advertising and promotion to the agency, considering it a wise move. Although the agency has only been open for a month, its daily workload is extremely busy.

Western Woman Loses Valuable Diamond Ring, Requests Investigation 129

A middle-aged Western woman named Guesse rents Room 207 on the second floor of the Broadway Mansions on Suzhou Road, Hongkou. The woman is over forty years old and usually dresses luxuriously and enjoys ornamentation. In addition to being surrounded by jewelry, she also has a platinum ring inlaid with emeralds, worth over six thousand gold coins, which she wears on her finger every day and never takes off. Yesterday afternoon, the woman took it off and placed it in a basin on the table in the room because it was inconvenient to wash. Unexpectedly, in a blink of an eye, the diamond ring had disappeared. She was greatly alarmed and immediately rang the bell to call the waiter to inquire, but the waiter replied that he did not know. Although a search was conducted everywhere, there was no trace of it. In desperation, the woman telegraphed the competent police station, which sent detectives to investigate, but they also found no clue. The waiter in charge of the room was then taken to the police station for questioning.

Notes on the Soviet Print Exhibition 132

— Lu Xun

I remember a time when we were rarely able to learn about the situation in the Soviet Union from domestic publications. Even in the realm of literature and art, some respectable writers and scholars avoided it like a young lady avoiding asphalt. Not only would they never touch it, but they would also keep their distance and wrinkle their noses. However, things have been different in the last year or two. Naturally, we occasionally still see a few satirical cartoons taken from foreign publications, but more often, we see sincere introductions of the achievements of construction. This makes people look up and see airplanes, water gates, workers' residences, and collective farms, instead of only looking at the ground, thinking about worn-out shoes, shaking their heads, and sighing. These introducers are not people with so-called dangerous political leanings, but they are definitely not gloating over disasters. Therefore, they are very happy to see the peace and prosperity of their neighbors and want to share this happiness with the Chinese people. I believe that this phenomenon is excellent for both China and the Soviet Union. On one hand, the truth is being revealed to us, allowing us to understand. On the other hand, there is no more misunderstanding, and it proves that there are indeed many people in China who "cannot be subdued by power or moved by poverty and humbleness" and who are determined to tell the truth.

However, these introductions are all articles or photographs. This year's print exhibition directly presents art before our eyes. Among the artists, several are familiar to us due to reproductions of their works, but seeing the handmade originals now makes us feel even closer.

Woodcut prints were invented in China long ago, but they declined in the middle of their history. The newly emerging woodcuts of the past five years take their inspiration from Europe and have no connection to ancient woodcuts. Soon, they were suppressed, and there was a lack of teachers, so there has been no particular progress to date. At this exhibition, we can find excellent and numerous models. First, we should pay attention to the master Favorsky, who reformed woodcut prints during the civil war and has been constantly moving forward since then, as well as his school of Deineka, Goncharv, Echerstov, Pikov, etc. Each of them expresses the spirit of truth in their works. We can see how their successors follow the path indicated by their teachers, but use different methods, which shows us that as long as the content is the same, the methods can vary, and that imitation and dependence can never produce true art.

The works of Deineka and Echerstov have not been introduced to China, and unfortunately, there are very few of them here. We have only seen one woodcut by Pavlinov, who is close to Favorsky, but this exhibition makes up for this lack.

Only one woodcut by Krarchnko was fortunate enough to be sent to China and reproduced and introduced. Now, everyone can see more of his original works. His romantic colors can stir the passion of our youth, and his attention to the background and meticulous expression will also benefit viewers. Our painting, since the Song Dynasty, has been dominated by "xieyi" (sketching the idea). Two dots are the eyes, without knowing if they are long or round. One stroke is a crow, without knowing if it is a magpie or a swallow. The pursuit of lofty simplicity has become emptiness. This flaw is still commonly seen in the works of young woodcut artists today. Krarchnko's new work "Dnerrostoruy (Construction in Nepal)" is a wake-up call to those lazy fantasies. As for Piskarev, he is probably the first woodcut artist to be introduced to China. His four illustrations of "The Iron Flood" have long been appreciated by many young readers, and now we see his illustrations for "Anna Karenina" - another aspect of his engraving style.

There are also Mrtiokhin, Khizhinsky, and Mochalov, who are all known to China in advance, as well as the works of many artists who are seeing for the first time. From artists who were already famous before the October Revolution to young artists born in the early 20th century, they are all demonstrating to us the path of cooperation and progress towards peaceful construction. Other artists and works are briefly explained in the exhibition booklet, and at the end, the overall point is revealed: "The general socialist content and the fundamental effort towards realism." There is no need for me to elaborate here.

However, we should also pay attention to the fact that there are works by artists from Ukraine, Georgia, and Belarus. I think that without the October Revolution, these works would not only not be able to meet us, but they might not even have appeared.

Now, more than two hundred works have appeared brilliantly together in Shanghai. In terms of prints alone, it seems to us that they are not as exquisitely woven as French works, nor as bold as German works. However, they are sincere without being stubborn, beautiful without being lascivious, pleasant without being ecstatic, and powerful without being crude. But they are not static either. They make people feel a kind of tremor - a tremor that is like the footsteps of a large army advancing towards the road of construction on solid, vast black soil, step by step, with firm steps.

Postscript: There are five types of prints in the exhibition: woodcuts, collographs (the catalog translates it as "oilcloth engraving," which is quite strange), and the names are self-explanatory. Two types are made by etching copper plates and lithographs with corrosive liquid. Translating them as "copper engraving" and "lithograph" is acceptable, or translating them as "etching" and "lithography," as in the catalog, is also acceptable. There is also a Monotyhe, which is created by painting on a plate and then printing on paper, so although it is a print, it is only a single piece. I think it can only be translated as "monotype print." The explanation in the exhibition booklet translates it as "Monotype," which is no better than not translating it. Sometimes it is translated as "Single Type Studies," which is even more difficult to understand than not translating it. In fact, the explanations without the authors' names are very concise and to the point, but unfortunately, the translation is very confusing. If someone re-translates it, it will still be very useful for those who pay attention to prints, even after the exhibition has closed.
