Chinese Vocational Education Society Held Expert Conference Yesterday, Experts Expressed Opinions on National Crisis Education, Special Education Changed to National Revival Education, and Initiated National Salvation Gold Savings Society 135

The Chinese Vocational Education Society held its 10th Expert Conference and Spring Review Conference at Shanghai University yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. The morning session included work reports and expert reviews and opinions. Lunch was at Shanghai University at noon, and the meeting continued at 1:30 PM to discuss the implementation plan for special education, etc. Details are recorded as follows:

Experts in Attendance

Including Niu Yongjian, Zhuang Zexuan, Tao Xingzhi, Ou Yuanhuai, Liu Zhanen, Chen Heqin, Chen Qingshi, Wang Zhuoran, Chen Jicheng, Zheng Xigu, Zhang Yousan, Yang Wei Wang, Jia Foru, Pan Yangyao, He Qingru, Lin Zhuoran, Yao Huiquan, Yang Chonggao, Shi She, Wen Chonglu, Xie Xiangzhi, Zhang Yi, Wang Sheng, Zhao Wu, Liang Zhongduan, Lin Meiyan, Zheng Wenhan, Xue Jianming, Wu Cui, etc., more than 40 people in total.

Work Report

Chairmen: Liu Zhanen, Zhuang Zexuan, Ou Yuanhuai; Stenographers: Zhu Zhongzheng, Cai Zhaolian. First, Yang Shuyu delivered the opening speech, followed by work reports. He Jirui reported on research and editing, Pan Yangyao reported on vocational guidance, Yao Huiquan reported on rural service, Yang Weiyu reported on design, Liang Zhongyuan and Zhao Wu reported on supplementary education, Jia Foru reported on the Chinese Vocational School, Xue Mingjian reported on the Labor Autonomous Region, and other temporary reports.

Experts' Opinions

After the work reports, the experts in attendance expressed their opinions on special education. Tao Xingzhi said that the name "Special Education Committee" was used specifically for bandit suppression in Jiangxi, Anhui, and Hubei. Our current discussion on special education may be misunderstood by others. The recent meaning of the Ministry of Education's organization of the Special Education Committee is to cope with the educational policy during the current national crisis period, which is the same as our discussion of new meanings. However, the national crisis education needed in China now should have several characteristics: a single goal, mass-oriented, connected, action-oriented, and official-driven. With the above principles, there is more basis, he said. Liu Zhanen said, "Today's discussion of national crisis education, I think we should come up with a plan that is simple and can be done. In my opinion, it should be divided into two aspects: spiritual and skill-based. The spiritual aspect can be divided into four points: the nation must have self-confidence, be brave, be organized, and be able to sacrifice," he said. Ou Yuanhuai said, "The Ministry of Education attaches importance to the broad sense of special education. It is not possible to have people without leaders, nor is it possible to have leaders without people. The people must be trained, and intellectuals must also be trained," he said. Zheng Xigu said that national crisis education is nothing more than spiritual training, physical training, and skill training. To implement this training, first, there must be strict military management; second, teachers and staff must set an example; third, there must be considerable preparation; and fourth, existing courses must be reduced, he said. Chen Heqin said, "The magnificent singing is most able to inspire young people's patriotic thoughts and national spirit, so songs are a very effective method for training young people." Zhang Yousan said, "It is very difficult for schools to have special inventions. The Academia Sinica should be responsible for special inventions." Zhuang Zexuan said that regarding youth training, in higher education, the engineering college must be fully utilized, students above high school should be trained to have command ability, and technical committees should be organized in various universities to undertake national defense research and implementation work. Chen Jicheng said, "Special education in schools is easy to train, and special training for the people is relatively indirect, so I believe that students should be responsible for organizing and training the people, which will be more effective." In addition, He Qingru, Chen Qingshi, and others also expressed their opinions, which are omitted for brevity.

Discussion of Proposals

The meeting continued at 1:00 PM to discuss the proposals. The implementation plan for special education was decided to be changed to the implementation plan for national revival education. The content of the plan from the sixth item onwards was summarized as physical training, spiritual training, skill training, and social activities, and an implementation committee was organized, the list of which was determined by the office. The main working policy for this year was determined, and it was decided to pay attention to the education plan during the extraordinary period. The location for the annual meeting was selected in accordance with the decision of the Du Member Congress. It was decided to choose between Nanning and Xi'an. A temporary motion was made to initiate the National Salvation Gold Savings Society of the Republic of China, which was passed. The meeting adjourned after the discussion. The declaration of national salvation savings is recorded as follows:

National Salvation Savings

The National Salvation Gold Savings Society of the Republic of China declares as follows: After several considerations and discussions, we have decided to initiate the "National Salvation Gold Savings Society of the Republic of China". The ten articles of association have been drafted, and all the purposes, organizational methods, etc., are detailed in them. We should also briefly explain the reasons for initiating this society. We all feel that a country and a nation can survive and support themselves on the land of fierce competition only if they rely on themselves to have a considerable amount of strength. This strength is manifested in culture, politics, economy, and other aspects, and the most important and precious one is the patriotic heart and unity of the entire nation. This can also be regarded as the engine for the development and advancement of all national power, and the nourishment for its prosperity and growth. Patriotic heart is inherent in everyone, and organizational power is not something that Chinese people lack innately. We believe that if we want to universally develop national patriotism and unity, we must have a concrete fact attached to it, because with this concrete fact, everyone can save money, everyone can practice frugality, and everyone can exercise self-discipline. Moreover, this concrete fact must be simple and easy to implement, and it must be easy to cover the entire population and easy to complete the organization. The country to which we entrust our lives has now reached a critical juncture of life and death. Who does not feel the danger? Who does not want to save the country and preserve its existence? However, everyone cannot think of an effective and universal method for a while, so everyone feels bored and anxious. In fact, there is more than one way to save the country. Specialized and general methods should be used in parallel, and it should be recognized that general methods are the basis of specialized methods. We believe that relying on a concrete fact to develop national patriotic enthusiasm and forge unity is the most common, most effective, and most universal method of saving the country. We initiated this society to unite the people of the whole country and create a broad and universal movement and organization by means of a concrete fact of "saving the country through saving money", so that everyone can get an opportunity to train themselves in group living habits, and everyone can develop a red heart to love the country and the nation. Speaking of the methods of this society, there are also several characteristics: Save your own money and keep it yourself, without entrusting others, and trusting your own personality; the amount of money saved is not limited, and it is extremely free; the name of the savings is set as "saving the country", which is simple and easy to understand; the basic organization can be realized anywhere; the joint organization is extremely natural, and the implementation method is not too expensive or difficult, and the large organization can be gradually completed along the natural trend. The patriotic atmosphere can gradually permeate the special environment, and unknowingly, a universal and great national power can be cultivated. This national power, in terms of spirit, is generated internally and strengthened, extremely substantial and not virtual. In terms of material, it is to accumulate a small amount to form a large number. The total number of the whole body may not be small. We believe that this method of saving the country is extremely common and mediocre, but only by being common can it be universally promoted throughout the country, and only by being mediocre can it be easily implemented by everyone in the country. All my comrades, let's get to work!

We must know that our country's culture has been very glorious for thousands of years. The previous strength was also due to culture. If we abandon the existing culture and do not talk about it today, how can we start in the spiritual aspect of saving the country? This is why Mr. Jiang is interested in this. The Shanghai Branch of the Law Society of the Republic of China Was Established Yesterday, and 17 Directors Were Re-elected 137

The Shanghai Branch of the Law Society of the Republic of China held its founding meeting at the Zhonghua Xueyi Du on Amars Road in the French Concession at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than 100 members attended. Tan Zhen, Xu Yuanhao, Shen Junru, Guo Wei, Jiang Yiping, etc. were publicly elected as the presidium, and Yuan Dingxin was the recorder. Details are recorded as follows:

Meeting Situation

After performing the ceremony, Chairman Tan Zhen reported on the preparations. Then, Lu Jingshi, the representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, briefly saying that the resolutions of the National Judicial Conference last year should be gradually implemented by the judicial authorities, and the Law Society organized by celebrities from all walks of life has the responsibility to supervise them. The abolition of consular jurisdiction is also an urgent matter. He also hoped that the society would conduct practical research. In short, the society has a major responsibility for the improvement of the judiciary, and it must achieve the rule of law advocated by the Three People's Principles, which is what is expected. Jiang Jianbai, the representative of the Education Bureau, gave a training speech, briefly saying that there are many social organizations, but very few have achieved results. The reason for this is probably that a group of people participate in a group at the beginning, and do not recognize the obligations that members should have. For example, academic groups should study academics, so that there is no contribution after joining the group, and even the meetings of the affiliated associations are not attended. This is a common problem for a group of people. He hoped that the society would eliminate this problem, work hard to promote the rule of law, and to establish a country under the rule of law, it is necessary to make all the people of the country know the law, etc.

Tan Zhen's Speech

Tan Zhen, the representative of the general society, gave a speech, briefly saying that in modern times, the judicial examinations are advocated and the social sciences are greatly despised. In fact, the social sciences are very related to the national politics and should be given equal importance. Since the establishment of the Republic of China, most of the laws in our country have been copied from foreign countries, so there is a criticism of cutting the feet to fit the shoes. We should carry forward the inherent national spirit of our country and not copy foreign countries. The legal system in China is very complicated now. There are Continental factions, Anglo-American factions, etc. We should establish a legal system and carry forward the spirit of our nation. I traveled to France for a year and was very impressed with the French Law Society. The French Law Society initially had only a few members, but now it has more than 170,000 members, which has a great contribution to politics. I hope that this society will make a contribution to the entire politics.

Re-election of Directors

Zhang Shizhao, Wu Jingxiong, He Shizhen, Shen Junru, Jiang Yiping, Guo Wei, Sun Hao Kun, Situ Qingxian, Liang Renjie, Zheng Yue, Sun Xiaolou, Shan Yuhua and other 17 people.

Children's Education Novel Little Men (1) (8) (5) 141

— Original by LouisaM, Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

After the sweeping work was done, he transported many carts of small wooden strips from the forest to the woodshed, and earned another dollar. Then Xiaobiao helped bind textbooks, worked overnight, and worked patiently and independently on each book under the guidance of Fu Lang. Later, he received his salary and was very satisfied. The crumpled banknote seemed to have a kind of brilliance in his eyes.

"Now, I have a dollar for each of them. I like to give the money to my mother myself, so she can see that I remember my father."

So Xiaobiao reverently paid a visit to his mother, who accepted his small savings as a priceless treasure. She wanted to treasure it and not move it easily, but Xiaobiao begged her to buy some useful items for herself and the girls - who he felt were entrusted to him to take care of - so she couldn't help but agree to his request.

This made him extremely satisfied. Later, although he sometimes temporarily shed his burden, the desire to help still existed and increased with age. He often said the words "my father" with a slightly boastful tone, and also often said, as if he was asking for a glorious title, "Don't call me Xiaobiao anymore. I am already John Brooke." With such a strong ambition and ardent hope, the ten-year-old boy began his struggling career, and inherited his legacy - the gentle thoughts of a clever and gentle father, and the legacy of an immortal reputation"...(End of this chapter)

Hubei Province Implements Universal Physical Education: Provincial Department Drafts Measures Submitted to Provincial Government for Record, Stipulating Annual General Inspection in May 149

(Hankou Correspondence) The Hubei Provincial Department of Education, having received a telegram from President Chiang stating that public physical education should be vigorously promoted, and that all civil servants in government agencies and faculty members in schools should select a sport or recreational activity to achieve universality, the Director of the Department, Cheng Qibao, upon receiving the order, drafted the "Outline of Measures for the Universal Implementation of Physical Education in Hubei Province." After being approved by the Provincial Government for record, it was circulated for compliance. The measures are divided into eleven articles: Government agencies and schools should organize after-work or after-school sports associations to handle the implementation of sports for employees of their respective agencies and faculty members of their respective schools. However, if the number of employees or faculty members in an agency or school is too small, they may merge with other agencies or schools in the same area. Individual sports may be promoted by the agency or school. The head of each agency and the principal of each school shall serve as the president of the aforementioned sports association, supervising the implementation of physical education by their respective employees or faculty members. The Provincial Sports Promotion Committee will send personnel to assess the implementation at any time. Those over the age of sixty may be excused from participation at their discretion. Wuchang and Hankou should appropriately add sports fields. Counties that have not yet established them should promptly establish them in accordance with the Provisional Rules for the Establishment of Sports Fields in Various Counties and Equipment Standards previously set by the Department of Education. To facilitate practice in both winter and summer, fitness rooms and swimming pools should be built in the Wuhan area as soon as possible. County governments in other counties should also prepare to build all-weather playing fields in their respective counties. Employees of government agencies and faculty members of schools must select one of the following sports for daily practice after work or after school: A. Ball sports, temporarily limited to soccer and basketball; B. Track and field; C. National martial arts; D. Equestrian archery; E. Calisthenics; F. Swimming; G. Recreation, temporarily set as ping-pong, shuttlecock kicking, rope skipping, bicycle practice, and fitness dance. Employees of government agencies and faculty members of schools who are skilled in sports must take turns providing guidance to other members of the public in sports at least twice a week for a reasonable amount of time. In order to review the results of the implementation of physical education throughout the province, the Provincial Government will hold a provincial sports meet every May, with each administrative region as a unit. Each region will hold a regional sports meet one month prior, with each county as a unit. The preliminary selection methods below the district level will be determined by each district based on the actual conditions of the counties under its jurisdiction. All sports fields and public education centers must hold various sports or recreational competitions according to the season. All government agencies and schools should jointly or individually hold various sports competitions. If there is no suitable equipment, they may use the existing public sports fields in the same area and may entrust the person in charge of the field to assist with everything. All government agencies and schools should utilize their existing staff or faculty members with sports experience and expertise to guide practice. If there are no such personnel available, other suitable personnel may be hired. In order to universally train teachers, the Department of Education may, during the summer vacation each year, utilize the facilities of the Provincial Public Sports Field to run summer sports training classes. Personnel from various agencies will be sent to attend the classes, and upon completion, they will return to their original agencies to take charge of sports guidance and improvement matters. (21st)

Volume 3, Issue 5: Diligent Sports Monthly Published, National Game Essay Contest Results Announced 150

Diligent Sports Monthly, the only regular sports publication in the country, Volume 3, Issue 5, has been published. The content of this issue is exceptionally rich. Here is a summary: The cover features sports photos of Qian Hangsu, Pan Yingchu, and Jiao Yulian, three outstanding female athletes from Shanghai Dongya Physical Education College, which are very beautiful. The pictorial section contains 24 active photos of the Yunnan Provincial Games and the latest freehand exercise diagrams, which are even more valuable. The forum section contains Shao Rugan's "A Few Words on What Kind of Sports Should Be Adopted as National Games in Our Country" and Yang Jiesheng's "Discussion on the Reform of Sports Terminology." The special essays include Wu Yunrui's "Methods to Strengthen the Body" and Chen Yuguang's "Sports Training and the Revival of the Nation." The answer announcement section includes Huang Jianxing's "Our Country Should Adopt Soccer as a National Game" (first place) and Zhuang Wenchao's "Our Country Should Adopt Basketball as a National Game" (second place). The academic section includes Ruan Weicun's "Basic Physiological Anatomy of Physical Education," Liu Chaode's "Key Points of Middle School Morning Exercise Teaching," He Zhihao's "Research on Elementary School Physical Education Achievement Assessment Methods," Deng Kanshun's "Armed Five-Item Sports Competition Method," and Jiang Rongqiao's "Discussion on the Functions and Integration of National Martial Arts." The investigation and history section includes Zhou Weizhuo's "Record of the Japanese Sports Investigation" and Jiang Huaiqing's "Brief History of World Games." Economic Special

From Bank Interest Rates to the Issue of Interest Rate Reduction 151

— Sheng Kezhong

I. Introduction

Since the business community petitioned the Ministry of Finance to reduce interest rates to alleviate the difficulties of industries, this issue has attracted widespread attention. However, to reduce lending rates, the prerequisite is the reduction of deposit rates, as the net interest earned by the banking industry comes from the difference between deposit and lending rates. A January 17th report stated that the banking industry will form a committee to specifically study the reduction of interest rates, stating:

"Banks' lending comes from absorbing deposits. If lending rates are reduced without reducing deposit rates, it will be impossible to operate. The current deposit rates... foreign banks' highest is about 5%, Chinese banks' highest is about 1% annual interest, and pawnshops' highest is about 1% monthly interest. As for lending rates, foreign banks, Chinese banks, and pawnshops' lowest is about 6%, and highest is about 1.2-3%, depending on the market's money supply. If implemented, there should be remedies for existing deposits and loans."

From the above situation, we can see that the banking industry is completely seeking the reduction of lending rates from the perspective of its own interests. In other words, reducing interest rates to ease the burden on industries is indeed desirable, but they cannot sacrifice their own interests. Therefore, they have no other choice but to seek a reduction in the interest rates of deposits, which are the source of 90% of their funds. As a result, the banking industry acts as an intermediary (or brokerage industry), seeking the completion of transactions between borrowers and lenders while enjoying commissions. However, in the situation where deposits are used by banking entrepreneurs for speculation, the banking industry must devise an appropriate method to satisfy depositors. Therefore, reducing interest rates is easy to say when industries are eagerly hoping for it, but it is not easy to implement in the banking industry. The following is a description of the general situation of interest rates of various banks in Shanghai, followed by a study of strategies for reduction.

II. Overview of Bank Interest Rates

Bank interest rates can be divided into two major categories: deposit and lending. Deposit rates can be further divided into ordinary deposit rates and savings deposit rates. They are described as follows:

(A) Ordinary Deposits

Time Deposits: This type of deposit is represented by 18 banks including Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, China Enterprise Bank, China Industrial Bank, Yongxiang Bank, Zhongfu Bank, China Bank, China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Siming Bank, Kenye Bank, Juxingcheng Bank, China Industrial Bank, Zhonghui Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, China National Products Bank, Hengli Bank, and Guohua Bank. The period ranges from three months to five years. The highest interest rate is 1.2% per annum, and the lowest is 4% per annum. The details are as follows:

Period　Highest　Lowest　Average

Demand Deposits: This type of deposit is represented by 10 banks including Bank of Communications, Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, Zhonghui Bank, Kenye Bank, Siming Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Tongshang Bank, Shanghai Women's Bank, and China Enterprise Bank. The highest interest rate is 4% per annum, but due to interest rate increases, it can also be as high as 5%. The lowest is 2%. Two banks offer 2%, five banks offer 3%, and three banks offer 4%.

(B) Savings Deposits

Various banks have many different names for savings deposits. In fact, they cannot be distinguished by fixed-term or demand deposits and must be classified according to the different deposit and withdrawal methods. The four most important types are described below.

Fixed Deposit with Zero Withdrawal: This type of deposit is represented by 20 banks including China Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Bank, Yanyue Bank, Siming Bank, Xinhua Bank, Donglai Bank, Dalu Bank, Guohua Bank, Kenye Bank, Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Zhonghui Bank, Quangong Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Hengli Bank, Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, China National Products Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jiangsu Bank, and Tongshang Bank. The minimum term is one year, and the maximum term is more than ten years. The lowest interest rate is 5% per annum, and the highest is 1.2% per annum. Details are shown in the following table:

Zero Deposit with Fixed Withdrawal: This type of deposit is represented by 23 banks including China Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Bank, Yanyue Bank, Siming Bank, Jincheng Bank, Xinhua Bank, Donglai Bank, Dalu Bank, China Industrial Bank, Guohua Bank, China Kenye Bank, Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Juxingcheng Bank, Zhonghui Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, Jiangsu-Zhejiang Bank, China National Products Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jiangsu Bank, and Tongshang Bank. The term is the same as the above, and the interest rate is a minimum of 6% and a maximum of 1.2%. Details are shown in the following table:

Deposit Principal with Interest Payments: This type of deposit is represented by 22 banks including China Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Bank, Yanyue Bank, Zhongfu Bank, Siming Bank, Jincheng Bank, Xinhua Bank, Dalu Bank, Guohua Bank, Kenye Bank, Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Juxingcheng Bank, Zhonghui Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, Jiangsu-Zhejiang Bank, China National Products Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jiangsu Bank, and Tongshang Bank. The length of the term is the same as the above two, and the interest rate is a minimum of 6% and a maximum of 1.1%. Details are shown in the following table:

Fixed Deposit with Fixed Withdrawal: This type of deposit is represented by 17 banks including China Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Bank, Zhongfu Bank, Jincheng Bank, Xinhua Bank, Dalu Bank, Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Juxingcheng Bank, Quangong Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Hengli Bank, China National Products Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jiangsu Bank, and Tongshang Bank. The time ranges from a minimum of three months to a maximum of more than ten years. The interest rate is a minimum of 5% and a maximum of 1.2%. Details are shown in the following table.

The above tables are based on statistics from the deposit regulations of exchange banks. The division of the length of the term is entirely based on facilitating statistics. In fact, the term limits of various banks are either stipulated to be over ten years or within ten years. Therefore, the highest and lowest interest rates in some tables do not increase with the lengthening of the term. The average is also affected by this. However, in general, they all comply with the principle that the term and interest rate are directly proportional.

Lending Rates

There are no fixed rules and regulations for the lending rates of various banks that can be statistically analyzed, because the level of interest rates depends entirely on the tightness of the financial market, the borrower's determination of the amount of capital value, the presence or absence of competition, the strength of payment ability, and the safety of the investment. The data obtained from the survey is listed in the following table:

Except for Bank of Communications, which did not indicate annual or monthly interest, and Zhejiang Industrial, which indicated annual interest, all others are monthly interest. If converted to annual interest, the minimum is 8.4% and the maximum is 1.44%. Although lending rates are determined at any time based on customer conditions and financial market conditions, it is worth studying what the highest and lowest lending rates of banks are in practice. The following data are compiled from the Zhonghang Monthly (August 24th) and the Financial Weekly of the Central Bank (various issues this year):

Agency　Loan Name　Interest Rate

Huai River Guidance Committee　Huai River Guidance Loan　6% per annum

Construction Committee　Jiangnan Railway Loan　8%

Jiangsu Province　Construction Loan　9% per annum

Jiangsu Province Warehouse Construction Loan　7.5% per annum

Jiangsu Province Water Conservancy Public Bond Loan　8% per annum

Jiangsu Province　Silkworm Seed Loan　10% per annum

Jiangsu Province　Huai River Guidance Continued Loan　8% per annum

Zhejiang Province　Highway Loan　9% per annum

Zhejiang Province　Autumn Tax Loan　10% per annum

Zhejiang Province　Local Public Bond Loan　8% per annum

Zhejiang Province　Local Public Bond Continued Loan　10% per annum

Hubei Province　Flood Disaster Public Bond Loan　9%

Shaanxi Province　Wei River Diversion Loan　8% monthly interest

The interest rates listed in the above table are all for government agencies' loans, which can only be used as our reference. It is impossible to search for and statistically analyze the interest rates for loans to industries.

Looking at the above tables, the high deposit rates of banks in our country far exceed the 1% mentioned in the 17th report. Those with a one-year term reach 1% per annum, and those with a three-year term reach 1.2% per annum. With deposit rates so high, it is appropriate that lending rates also reach 1.2% per month. A recent report quoted a certain person in the financial community as saying that banks absorb deposits at high interest rates and speculate in foreign exchange and public bonds, which are profitable and have simple procedures, unlike investing in industries, which requires investigation and research and is less profitable and more complicated. In a few words, the attitude of the banking community is fully depicted.

If the banking industry in our country continues to plan for its own interests, absorbs deposits at high interest rates to engage in speculative activities, there is no need to reduce interest rates - and it is fundamentally impossible. If it embraces the spirit of co-existence and co-prosperity, it should automatically reduce interest rates without waiting for the industries to call for it, so that the industries can have access to low-interest capital.

III. Standard Highest and Lowest Interest Rates

The level of interest rates does not need to be restricted, and its trend depends entirely on the financial season and the demand between borrowers and lenders. If interest rates must be limited by laws and regulations, it is mostly an improper intervention in creditors, and the result may only cut off the financing channels for those who lack capital. Moreover, who can give up where interest lies? In fact, it is also difficult to take effect. Therefore, the so-called standard high and low interest rates in this section have two meanings: one is to prohibit absorbing deposits at high interest rates, and the other is the highest standard for lending rates. The level of interest rates must also depend on the level of domestic civilization. If the level of civilization is high, the people's knowledge will be advanced, the financial institutions will be complete, and people will not suffer from high interest rates. If the opposite is true, people will suffer from high interest rates. Our country's education bureau has not been popularized, and there is a traditional high-interest loan system. In addition, banks have absorbed deposits at high interest rates in recent years, so in fact, an appropriate interest rate must be set as a transitional measure. Secondly, the current lending rates in our country are also quite inconsistent. For example, the interest rates for loans to government agencies are as low as 6% per annum and as high as 1% per annum, while the interest rates of various banks obtained from the survey are mostly 8% to 1.2% per month. Secondly, the industries are now demanding a reduction in interest rates, so the degree of reduction must also have a limit at present, so that both can benefit. For these two reasons, it is impossible not to set a standard highest and lowest interest rate.

However, this standard is quite difficult to formulate, as it is feared that it will be too low or too high. Based on the average situation of the above tables, the following high and low interest rates are drafted:

(1) Ordinary Deposit Rates: The nature of this type of deposit is different from that of savings deposits, and the interest rate should be lower. The highest standard is set as shown in the table:

Term　One Year　Two Years　Three Years　Four Years　Five Years

Interest Rate　6.00%　6.％　6.0％　6.7％　7.00%

(2) Savings Deposit Rates: The trend of the above averages is that the increase in the early years is faster than in the later years. This table is also the same, and the highest standard is set as shown in the table:

Term　One Year　Two Years　Three Years　Four Years　Five Years

Interest Rate　6.00%　6.50%　7.00%　7.23%　7.5%

Six Years　Seven Years　Eight Years　Nine Years　Ten Years　Ten Years or More

7.75%　8.00%　8.25%　8.50%　8.75%　9.00%

(3) Lending Rates: A. 6% to 8% monthly interest; B. 5% to 7% monthly interest.

Deposit rates are generally based on one year. The rates for those within one year can be determined by the banks themselves, but the highest cannot exceed 6% for those with a term of nine months. Also, only the highest is set and not the lowest, because the current issue is a reduction problem, and it is not necessary.

As for lending rates, it is heard that a certain bank is only offering 5% monthly interest for special collateral loans to help industry and commerce. Also, according to the book "Operating Standards for Cotton Spinning Mills" published by the Cotton Industry Control Committee of the National Economic Commission, the interest expense is set at 7% or 8% per annum. Therefore, drafting the lending rate at 5% to 8% monthly interest is probably not too high or too low. However, this standard is still much higher than that of various advanced countries.

IV. Measures to Implement Interest Rate Reduction

The problem that arises in implementing interest rate reduction is not in the lending rate, but in the deposit rate, and in fact, it is even more in the attitude of the banking community. Because there is no problem with deposits and loans that have not been established during implementation, the problem lies in the remedial measures for established deposits and loans. Should we handle them according to the original agreement? Or should we revise the new agreement? If we follow the first rule, the bank will not prevent depositors from withdrawing and can safely use their funds. However, future lending can only be lent at low interest, and as a result, the bank may lose money. The first method is beneficial to the bank in preventing withdrawals, but high-interest absorption and low-interest lending are harmful to the bank. If we follow the second rule, the bank will inevitably face the withdrawal of depositors, but with low deposit interest and low lending interest, the bank can make a profit. The second method is harmful to the bank in terms of depositors' withdrawals, but low-interest absorption and low-interest lending are beneficial to the bank. It seems that the two methods have their own advantages and disadvantages. In fact, I think it is better to revise the new agreement. Why? Depositors will not necessarily withdraw. Because:

If bank interest rates are reduced uniformly, if you deposit in Bank A at this interest rate, you will also deposit in Bank B at this interest rate, and there will be no special treatment.

If you deposit in a merchant, the depositor's confidence in the merchant is not as strong as in the bank. The level of interest rate does not outweigh the safety of investment.

If you deposit in a foreign bank, the bankruptcy of foreign banks has been reported from time to time in recent years, and many Chinese people have suffered, which is not enough to inspire confidence among the Chinese people.

If you deposit to invest in real estate bonds, depositors who can invest in these two will never deposit the funds in the bank. Depositors who deposit in the bank have no great interest in investing in real estate bonds. This can be asserted.

Therefore, in my opinion, it is better to handle all old and new deposits and loans in accordance with the new standards.

V. Conclusion

Reducing interest rates to help industry and commerce is undoubtedly important. However, there are several issues that should be paid attention to after implementation, one is the general prohibition of high interest rates, and the other is the strict prevention of speculation. With regard to the former, there are currently many general stores, small companies, and small banks that offer 1% monthly interest for deposits with a one-year term, and it is inevitable that people will be confused by the high interest rates and forget the risks and fall into them. Therefore, it is necessary to strictly prohibit it. With regard to the latter, not only must the speculation of the banking industry be prohibited, but also the speculation of industry and commerce must be absolutely prohibited. The high interest rate is entirely due to the very high profits of speculation. If the speculation is popular, the banking industry will not hesitate to raise interest rates to engage in speculation, and as a result, the lending rates for industry and commerce will naturally be high. Therefore, speculation must be strictly prohibited.

I have no in-depth study of banking practice. This article is entirely based on the perspective of statistics to study the reduction of interest rates. Whether it is appropriate or not is still subject to experts' corrections.

The Benefits of Establishing a Central Land Bank 152

— Huang Angong

My previous suggestion to the central government to establish a Central Land Bank to promote China's land reform movement and develop China's land economy and credit has been adopted and passed at the Fifth Plenary Session. The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Interior have been instructed to handle the matter. I am deeply impressed! Although preparations for the Central Land Bank have been reported in the newspapers, when will we see the reality? What is the preparation plan? Will it be carried out entirely according to my suggestions, or will there be changes? So far, nothing has been heard. The establishment of the Central Land Bank is a new initiative for the country and society. It lacks established laws to follow and experience to draw on. Undertaking such a major and difficult task, if not done carefully, could have adverse effects. Therefore, I venture to offer a word as a warning.

I believe that the establishment of the Central Land Bank is not only to establish a new foundation for China's land reform movement. From the perspective of the national finances, the establishment of the Central Land Bank can first realize the new trend of creating capital by monetizing China's real estate. Secondly, it can discover a vast source of land credit capital that is inexhaustible in China's extremely weak and depleted financial resources. Thirdly, it can make agricultural financial activities easier to carry out, improve land, thereby rapidly increase land value, and promote agricultural production and industrial construction. All of these, directly and indirectly, are sufficient to increase government tax revenue and open up huge financial sources. Finally, the Ministry of Finance can establish this type of bank without raising a large amount of capital, but instead reap the creation of huge and stable capital. Therefore, I believe that the establishment of a land bank is not only a plan to reform China's land, but also a major plan to transform China's finances.

As for the establishment of the Central Land Bank, as mentioned earlier, it is an unprecedented initiative. Its organization is also very different from ordinary industrial and commercial banks. Moreover, specialized talents for this type of land bank are rare in China. Even Japan has not yet established a land bank. In this situation, how can the organization of the land bank give full play to its various strengths and functions? How should land bonds be issued? To what extent should the amount of land bonds issued be equivalent to the real needs of society? How should the lending system be determined? How should corporate finance be raised? How should practitioners be recruited and trained? All of these issues will be the most difficult problems in the current preparation for the Central Land Bank. These are all prerequisites for the establishment of a land bank, which is what we expect.

Land banks originated and flourished in Germany. The author had a special article introducing them in the local weekly published in the Central Daily News. In other words, Germany is the birthplace of land credit banks. People there have the most significant achievements in the organization, management, and operation of this type of bank, and they have abundant talents and experience. Therefore, the organizational system of land banks there is most worthy of our reference and attention. Therefore, I believe that at the beginning of the preparation of the Central Land Bank, in order to be cautious about the function and application of land banks, and for the sound development of the cause, and for the easy establishment of the bank, it is best to directly send people to Germany to conduct more practical research and investigation, or directly hire one or two German land credit experts to come to China to guide us, so that our country can get help from Mount Tai. Then the cause will be easy to achieve, and at the same time, it can reduce some of the adventurous nature of experimentation. This is also what we expect.

Although what has been said above is only to contribute opinions to the authorities, I believe that the establishment of the Central Land Bank is not only closely related to the government authorities, but also has a great impact on China's banking industry. I am afraid that the banking industry in China does not recognize the cause and effect of this, so I offer a few words for reference. In the past, China's banking system was based on cash reserves. Although this system can be said to be a stable and safe system in theory, in practice, cash is stored dead in the cellar, and useful cash and silver are placed in a useless place. It is not in line with the principle of economics, and it does not need economists to say it. Moreover, when the country is in a difficult diplomatic situation, once an international war breaks out, the bank will be attacked by the enemy, or they will first seize our cash reserves. At this time, although there is circulation of banknotes in the society, it will inevitably be equivalent to empty promises. As a result, on the one hand, it will be enough to cause the collapse of the national financial institutions, and on the other hand, it will inevitably lead to the defeat of wartime finance and put the war in a disadvantageous position. This is because the currency wars (Wahrungskrieg) of various countries have become increasingly fierce in recent years, and the system of using gold and silver is constantly changing. The lack of stability of this currency system is most likely to cause the bankruptcy of the cash reserve system. For example, the United States' change to the gold and silver standard and the implementation of the silver purchase policy immediately triggered a large outflow of silver from our country, causing great danger to the banks in Shanghai. Even American banks went bankrupt because of this. This is a clear indication of the weakness of the cash reserve banking system. Fortunately, since last year, the financial authorities have deeply realized that this system cannot be delayed for a long time, and resolutely promulgated a new plan for currency reform and implemented the legal tender system. This measure has been able to save the weakness of the existing banking system, but it has not been able to achieve a completely thorough reform of the banking cash reserve system. The former is the distribution of reserves, and now it is the concentration of reserves only. In the end, it still needs cash, and it still cannot avoid the various dangers listed above, so it cannot be regarded as a completely new banking system.

However, the land bank system that I suggest can completely abolish the cash reserve system and use land representing the value of capital as a reserve. This kind of land asset reserve cannot be plundered by thieves, nor can it be smuggled by the enemy, and water and fire cannot harm it. Currency wars cannot do anything to it. After the land is used as a bank fund, it can continue to be used and freely produced, completely eliminating the absolute violation of the principle of economics, which is to store cash dead in the cellar and spend insurance money and security costs. This is truly the safest system in the world, and the most economical way. Moreover, China is the country with the weakest and most lacking cash capital. Although there are gold and silver mineral resources in the country's land, there has been a lack of management to set up factories for mining, so it is quite difficult to meet the country's need for gold and silver or to raise funds for large banks. If it comes from borrowing foreign debts, on the one hand, it will promote the power of foreigners to invade China's economy, and on the other hand, it will be subject to high interest rates and harsh political or economic conditions, making China forever a debtor country in the international community. There are too many disadvantages to us to enumerate. Only because of this, China's banking industry will never have the possibility of great development. For example, the largest bank in China now, such as the Central Bank, only has 20 million yuan of capital. However, the national banks of the United Kingdom and the United States all exceed 500 million or 1 billion of capital, which is a world of difference. The reason is that my country's capital is poor, and the cash reserve banking system is not easy to promote. The United Kingdom and the United States have abundant domestic gold and silver production, and cash is sufficient. It is not difficult to gather 100 million or 1 billion of bank capital. This is due to the economic substance of society, not that our intelligence and talent are not as good. On the contrary, if China can now promote the new land bank system, it can completely avoid the aforementioned restrictions and influences of various disadvantages. Especially without begging for foreign aid, it is the most effective way for China to strengthen itself, be self-reliant, self-help, strive, self-sufficient, and save itself. The promotion of the land bank system will never be hindered by China's lack of cash. The capital required by this type of bank is not cash but land. Therefore, the larger the area and value of the land, the easier it is to accumulate the capital of the land bank. My country is the country with the largest land area in the world. If we can organize banks according to this principle, then our country can establish the greatest bank in the world. Taking Shanghai as an example, if we can cooperate to form a land bank with all the real estate in Shanghai, such as the German Stadtschaften, we can get more than 2 billion of land capital. Re-estimating the value of the real estate in Nanjing, it is also a huge amount of more than 1 billion yuan. If we can organize a bank in this way, we can generate the largest bank in the world without begging for a penny of foreign debt. In the past, we did not plan this and abandoned it on the ground, and still said that the country's financial resources are poor. What a mistake! Therefore, in order to improve China's banking organization and open up a way for self-reliance, I deeply hope that the banking industry in China will recognize the characteristics and great functions of the land bank. On the one hand, we should try our best to assist in the preparation of the Central Land Bank. On the other hand, within the possible scope, the banking industry may also organize more of this type of bank to promote the utilization of land credit in China. According to the author's observation, because the organization of a land bank does not require cash as a reserve, a land bank can be organized not only in the city but also in the countryside. The best way is to take the township as a unit and use cooperative methods for all the land in each township, such as organizing it according to the German Landschaften. In this way, there are 300,000 villages in China, which can form 300,000 land cooperative banks. Assuming that the capital of each land bank is 5,000 yuan, then the total land capital in China can be 1.5 billion yuan. In this way, the country can be covered with a bank network, opening up a great way for the development of the banking industry. At the same time, with the relief and circulation of 1.5 billion yuan of land credit in the rural areas, the current extremely serious financial problems in the rural areas can be solved. Only then can the revitalization of the rural areas and the revival of the national movement be expected to achieve true success.

Securities 153

After the Reopening of the Securities Market, Prices Only Saw a Brief Rebound, Falling by About Two to Nine Yuan

From February 17th to 22nd last week, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, after a 16-day closure, finally reopened. After going through various difficulties, there was a sincere fear of a sharp decline after the reopening. After much effort, the Ministry ordered temporary regulations: short sellers were required to deliver the actual goods, new short selling was temporarily suspended, and the existing spot trading in the market was also temporarily suspended. The doors to short selling were completely closed, while those who went long were treated as before. After buying on the same day, selling on the same day was not accepted by the exchange. The above measures to maintain the market were indeed effective. However, brokers had extreme difficulties in settling accounts for customers. It was faintly heard that most of them advised the short side to make up for the losses first, and then the long side could sell. This clever method was used to avoid disputes. However, after the reopening, the market price still plummeted, with great fluctuations. At present, the delivery period is near, and according to the usual practice, there is only one day. The exchange has not yet announced whether it will be extended by one or two days to facilitate the closing. Whether the March futures will be listed, and when the unified public bonds will be auctioned are all uncertain. It is faintly heard that the March futures will not be auctioned, and the unified public bonds will be auctioned in April and May. Whether this is true remains to be verified. At present, the short sellers have all delivered the goods. The strength of the long side is unknown. With banks reducing deposit interest rates and the exchange providing collateral loans, the long side is relatively stable. However, the short side is still confident. The turbulence will only subside after the delivery of the February futures. Last week, the Ministry ordered the reopening on Monday, but the brokers requested various things and failed to open on time. It was delayed until 4:30 pm before the first session was opened. The market price plummeted, falling by about four yuan. However, the suspension board was not displayed, and it was maintained repeatedly. It still plummeted because the market price was too high and did not match the ratio of the unified public bonds. On Tuesday, the exchange issued a notice requiring short sellers to deliver all the actual goods before 12:00 noon. The brokers were very crowded when delivering the goods. The exchange took time to inspect and collect the goods, and it was still delayed until 4:30 pm before another session was opened. The market price was still sluggish, and it fell sharply to the suspension board, a small three yuan or so. Only 20 closed up to four jiao. On Monday, the exchange made up for the short sellers who failed to deliver the actual goods. There were two sessions in the morning and afternoon, and the market price rebounded by one jiao to two yuan or so. On Thursday, the transaction volume decreased significantly, and the full-day four sessions were restored. Because the short sellers delivered the goods, the long side began to sell, and it rebounded by a small number of jiao to one yuan and six jiao. On Friday, the long side continued to come out, and the short side was determined to hold on. Prices fell again, with a fall of two yuan and seven jiao for some, and at least five jiao for others. On Saturday, foreign banks reduced deposit interest rates, and the exchange provided collateral loans at 80% of the value. The long side's line was slightly strengthened, rising by one jiao to one yuan and three jiao. As the date gets closer, the changes are likely to be yet to come. As a result of the week's market price, it fell by seven yuan to nine yuan or so compared to January 29th, which can be said to be a strange change in recent years. Grain: River Rice Sales Slightly Active 154

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than 20 sources from various gangs, with more than 4,000 shih of goods. On the sales side, since the rainy weather of the previous dynasty, transactions have been scarce. Yesterday, there was a slight movement on the street, with more than 1,000 packages of thin rice and more than 300 packages of thick rice being handled by the Baowei, Longkou, and Qingdao gangs. Therefore, the situation was slightly tight, and the market conditions were good. The price of thick early japonica rice rose by several fen to nearly one jiao, and the price of thin rice increased by five fen to one jiao. Duyang pointed rice increased by about one jiao, and the price of Bianyuan high-quality rice was also good.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were 22 or 23 sources from various routes down the river. The market for white japonica rice was slightly more active, and the price rose by several fen. The retail of early thin rice was still acceptable, and the market price increased by nearly one jiao. The retail sales of Yangjian rice were slightly active, and the price increased by about one jiao. Dujian was stable, and the retail sales of Baiyuan and Yinyuan rice continued to be handled, and the price turned tighter by several fen. The prices of other goods also stood firm.

Sugar Market: Actual Sales Were Sluggish, and the Sugar Market Continued to Weaken 155

Yesterday, the foreign currency market continued to weaken due to sluggish actual sales. The Association marked the spot price of Grade 24 coarse white sugar at 22.4 yuan, which was slightly lower by 1 jiao compared to the 21st. Although the price of transshipment goods held at the original price of 7.4 yuan, it was heard that the dark market had loosened, and the weakening trend seemed to be continuing. The spot price of East Red Grade 8 white sugar was 22.05 yuan, and the price of transshipment goods was 7.05 yuan, both slightly lower by 5 fen. The quoted price of Grade 9 YRO was the same as before, but the acceptance rate was low, and there were signs of further weakening. The price of the factory's refined white sugar loosened with the price of coarse white sugar, also slightly lower by 1 jiao. The price of Zhenji Grade 1 was 21.2 yuan, Grade 2 was 21 yuan, Grade 3 was 20.8 yuan, Grade 4 was 6 jiao, and Grade 5 was 4 jiao. Although the makers of domestically produced Qingchi sugar insisted on their prices, the sales have been quiet in recent days, and there is a general feeling that it is difficult to rise or fall.

Survey: Shanghai Price Index for January 156

According to the report of the National Fixed Tariff Commission, compared with the previous month, the Shanghai wholesale, export, and import price indexes and the Shanghai living expenses index in January of the 25th year all rose slightly except for a slight decrease in imports. Although the foreign exchange market price did not change this month, the overseas silver price plummeted. The Shanghai British Exchange market price was still one shilling, two pence, and three hundred and seventy-five li, while the London silver price fell from two shillings and six pence and four hundred and thirty-seven li in the previous month to two shillings in this month. When the parity of the British exchange is one shilling, four pence and three hundred and thirty-one li, and the foreign exchange was lower than the parity by twelve percent last November, since the collection of silver export tax, balance tax in the 23rd year and the implementation of the legal tender last November, the relationship between our country's prices and overseas silver prices has not been as close as in the past. The reason why the index change this month is still stable is probably due to this.

Wholesale Price Index: The total index was 104.3, an increase of 1.0% compared with the previous month and an increase of 4.9% compared with the same month last year. Compared with the previous month, all the eight types of indexes rose except for a slight decrease in the metal category. The increase in building materials was relatively large, followed by fuel textiles and grains. The increase in the remaining three categories did not exceed 0.8%. The building materials category index increased by 3.9%. The prices of Douglas fir and Liu'an planks both increased due to high overseas prices. The prices of lime, black bricks, etc. were also strong. The fuel category index increased by 1.8%. Firewood rose sharply due to scarce arrivals, and charcoal increased due to the relatively smooth winter sales. The textile category index increased by 1.4%. After the price of white cloth rose month by month from July and August last year, it was slightly fatigued last month. This month, due to insufficient inventory, retailers held firm, and the market price rebounded. The price of white ramie also rose due to slight movements in exports. Various cotton yarns mostly rose due to the purchase of various gangs. However, cotton prices were uniformly weak and fell due to the closure and reduction of work by yarn factories at the end of the old lunar year and the decrease in raw material demand. The grain category index increased by 1.1%. The rise and fall of the rice market were mixed. Although Dumi fell in price due to the surge in arrivals and sluggish sales, foreign rice was firm due to the lack of arrivals and inventories and the increase in reports from the place of origin. Domestic wheat is waiting for new production, and the existing inventory is small, and the factory demand is strong, and the opening price has risen sharply. Flour is expensive due to the cost of raw materials, and the movements of various gangs are endless, and the market is firm. The metal category index fell by 2.9%. Various hardware transactions were even quieter during the settlement period, and sales prices mostly fell.

Export Price Index: The total index was 90.8, an increase of 0.9% compared with the previous month and an increase of 17.6% compared with the same month last year. Compared with the previous month, the three types of indexes, consumer goods, fell slightly, and raw materials and finished products all rose slightly. The consumer goods index fell by 0.1%. The prices of various products rose and fell by half, but the prices of the major exports of red and green tea, egg white, and lard all fell, probably due to sluggish foreign sales. The raw materials index rose by 1.1%. Ramie and coal dust both rose due to demand exceeding supply. The inventory of pig bristles was weak, and Europe and the United States made purchases, and the selling price was super expensive. Yellow soybeans and small tin ore also rose. The finished product index rose by 1.1%. Various warps were uniformly expensive. Asphalt opened at a higher price because foreign companies and soap factories moved in droves. (To be continued)

Chunqiu

Tidbits 157

— (Tiewu)

A person coming out of the womb is like an athlete crossing the finish line in a race. On this road, there is a clear dividing line that defines the scope of your actions. You carefully walk within the track to the finish line, and many people will agree with you, admire you, and imitate you. If you are not careful and cross the line, not only will all your previous efforts be in vain, but you will also be blamed and laughed at. "One wrong step can cause eternal regret." Those who walk the road should take care of themselves.

The journey of life, at most, lasts a hundred years. On this short journey, you should leave a trace for those who come after you to admire, so that they know that there was someone like you who walked this road, so that you will not have wasted your hundred years.

A Record of the Burial of an Unknown Hero 158

— Liutang

The tomb of the unknown hero of Shanghai City has been completed, and the unveiling ceremony was held on February 16. Earlier, at 10:00 am on the 9th, the remains of the fallen soldiers were buried near Miaohang, in a place called Sanbai Mudi. The Battle of Miaohang was one of the most intense battles in the Shanghai War. The Japanese army poured in its elite troops, bringing its new-style weapons with them. For a time, our troops suffered many casualties. Afterwards, fresh troops were transferred to succeed them, and the original positions were retaken. On the day of the final retreat of the troops, the Japanese army could not cross the Lei Chi line, which was also a heroic feat.

After the incident, the Shanghai Tongren Fuyuantang searched for the remains and buried them separately. This time, wanting to examine a skeleton from among them and move it to the Tomb of the Unknown Hero, the Shanghai Disabled People's Hospital sent someone to grope and designate it. The person who groped was slightly knowledgeable about astrology and took the matter quite seriously, searching in the dark east and west, and walking north and south. Finally, on the tomb site at the original entrance, he designated a skeleton. There were sixty-seven others buried in the same place, this being one of the sixty-seven coffins.

What is strange is that not all of the coffins are nameless. When the Tongren Fuyuantang buried them, if they encountered a symbol on the chest that could identify the surname and department, they engraved it on the tombstone to prepare for their descendants to come and recognize it. The method was very complete. Only the skeleton designated by the person who groped had no surname that could be examined. What was presented to the eyes when the coffin was opened was a purplish-red skeleton, missing its left arm and left leg. Therefore, it was enshrined in a stone coffin, the coffin was lined with gray powder, a yellow silk mattress was laid, the skeleton was placed on top, and it was covered with a silk quilt. Then the lid was sealed tightly and moved to the Tomb of the Unknown Hero.

There are those who are knowledgeable about feng shui who say that the bones of the deceased are usually gray-white, and those that turn purple must have prosperous descendants. If so, this is also Heaven's way of rewarding loyal souls!

On the day of the unveiling ceremony, in the afternoon, thousands of people went to pay their respects, and the enthusiasm was unprecedented. Many brought tin foil to burn, which shows the depth of their admiration.

The Confucian Temple Park 159

— Rong Yu

In the past, when going to Nanshi for a stroll, there was only the City God Temple. The incense there was thick, the market sounds were noisy, and those who loved quietness found it a bit too much to bear. Now there is the Confucian Temple Park, which is clean and noble, surpassing the City God Temple by many times. No wonder tourists flock to it. That's right! There are flowers, plants, trees, pavilions, stones, and ponds there, and the scenery is beautifully decorated. Moreover, there are books and newspapers to read, and various models and antiques are displayed, which is enough to broaden your horizons and increase your knowledge. Several friends in the city who love to listen to books can also listen to good books and drink cheap tea when they get inside. So I often joke with my friends, if I lived in Nanshi, I would definitely move near the Confucian Temple and sit there for a few hours in the morning and evening, which would be much more refreshing than being locked in a guest room. Moreover, across the street is the zoo, where you can listen to the birdsong and ape cries, and watch the fish swimming and the beasts jumping, which is also a happy thing. So I don't go to Nanshi often, but when I do, I always go inside for a few hours.

The current Confucian Temple Park is quiet in the midst of the hustle and bustle, and tourists are as thick as crucian carp. But talking about the situation twenty-five years ago is not the same. At that time, the city walls of Shanghai had not yet been demolished, and the traffic between the concession and the city relied on several city gates for entry and exit, which was not very convenient. Especially the area around Ximen was unusually desolate. In the area around the Confucian Temple, not to mention at night, even during the day, few people passed by. At that time, the gate of the Confucian Temple was still an old-fashioned building, with a black lacquered gate painted with deities and a threshold several feet high. Except for the spring and autumn sacrifices, it was always closed all year round. In front of the gate was a screen wall; in front of the gate was a vegetable garden; in the west corner, the Kuixing Pavilion stood tall; in the middle, the Dacheng Hall had moss growing on its four walls; a pool of water was also green all year round. At that time, those who went in only felt a sense of solemnity tinged with desolation. Who would have thought that after a series of reforms, after being converted into a park, the Dacheng Hall is still the Dacheng Hall, the Kuixing Pavilion is still the Kuixing Pavilion, the ponds are still the same, and the trees are unharmed, but the scenery is very different. Culture is evolving and progressing, and I have the same feelings about the present and the past of the Confucian Temple!

Those who Cannot Create are the Best at Enjoying

——Reflections on the "Escalator" at Shanghai's Da Sun Company

Little Western Paradise 160

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Four: Weighing Profit, Love is Lightly Tossed; Husband Sacrifices Affection; Lofty Ambition, Strong Legs Venture to the Wilderness

Wang Shicheng, seeing that he was being treated very courteously, couldn't very well directly refuse him. He picked up his cup, took a sip, smacked his lips, and said with a smile, "Although Mr. Jia is interested in our piece of land, it's rare for a buyer to contact the sellers like this. Considering our relationship with Mr. Jia, we'll try our best to make this happen." As he spoke, his eyes glanced toward Bei Hai. Bei Hai, holding his wine cup, had a faint smile on his face, clearly not taking Shicheng's words seriously. Jia Duocai silently drank a couple of cups of wine and said to Shicheng with a smile, "I understand this piece of land isn't entirely up to you two, but if you're both willing to contribute some ideas, I think this deal can be made. I won't lie, I really want these two pieces of land, and I hope you two can help me out a bit." Shicheng looked at Bei Hai, smiled for a moment, but didn't say anything. Jia Duocai laughed, "I know the key to all of this lies with Brother Bei Hai alone. If Brother Bei Hai is willing to take on some responsibility, this matter is sure to succeed nine times out of ten." As he spoke, his right hand held the wine pot, and his right elbow leaned on the table as he stared intensely at Bei Hai. Naturally, his face still carried a smile. Bei Hai picked up a salted duck egg with its shell, placed it in front of him, held the eggshell with the index finger of his left hand, and slowly picked at the egg white with his chopsticks. Then he smiled faintly, "Mr. Jia, it's no use putting such a high hat on me. I'm just a clod, and a high hat would just wobble and fall off." Jia Duocai completely forgot to entertain his guests, picked up the wine pot himself, poured himself a cup of wine, tilted his head back, and drank it as if to embolden himself with the wine. As the wine went down, he straightened his chest, put on a serious face, then smiled again, and said in a deep voice, "Brother Bei Hai, you're not married yet, are you? I have some good news for you. That Miss Zhu Yueying, I've... freed her. If Brother Bei Hai is interested, this would be a very good match." Bei Hai slammed his wine cup down, blushed, and stood up, saying, "Mr. Jia, what are you saying? Do you think..." Jia Duocai immediately grabbed him, pressed him down, and said with a laugh! "I've had a couple of extra drinks, so I'm talking a bit loosely. But I think very highly of you, considering you a fine young man, and I'm very willing to be your friend." (406)

Special Feature of This Publication

A Tour of the Qimei Road Public Housing Village 161

— Yafei

Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four essential elements of life, but in Shanghai, the housing problem is the most difficult to solve. Not only is the environment complex and the air polluted, affecting physical and mental health, but the high cost of rent is a real burden for the general salaried and working classes. However, for the sake of survival, these problems remain unsolved.

Recently, the municipal government, recognizing this situation, built four public housing villages last year on Qimei Road, Zhongshan Road, Damuqiao, and Pushanqiao in the city. The construction of each site has been completed in order, and residents have gradually moved in.

In order to learn more about the conditions in the village, I made a special trip to tour the Qimei Road public housing village one cold morning. The village is located on the small side of the second bridge on Qimei Road, facing the sun, so it is quite warm. There are two entrances, similar in style to the gates of a public school or campus. In the center are the auditorium, the office, and the reading room. The buildings are in a herringbone shape, with two flagpoles in front of the door, each displaying a banner, as well as a newspaper board and a bulletin board. Across from them is a square that serves as a sports field. The village has a total of 260 houses, divided into types A and B. Type A costs three yuan, and Type B costs four yuan. The structure of the houses is extremely simple and tidy. Each house is connected to a maximum of five or six families, with space left in front, behind, and on both sides for planting flowers and trees. Not only is there ample light and air circulation inside, but also, because fire hydrants and water dragons are set up everywhere, it is very safe. Each of the four corners of the village has a public toilet and a tap water pool. Each tap water pool is divided into more than ten compartments, each equipped with a tap. Next to it is a cement washing platform more than ten feet long, where more than ten people can wash things at the same time. The roads in the village are all paved with cement, and streetlights are installed at every corner. At night, there are police officers patrolling the village all night, so the villagers can live in peace.

Behind the auditorium is a consumer cooperative, which, in addition to supplying daily necessities, also has men's and women's bathrooms, as well as a public tea garden. Finally, there is the women's toilet.

There is a small school in the village, with an attached kindergarten. Children of villagers aged four to eight can enter the kindergarten, and those aged eight to sixteen can enter the primary school section. Tuition is completely free; only the cost of books is charged.

The equipment and organization of the village are very strict and tidy. All the living equipment in each house, such as electric lights and stoves, are installed completely by them. Residents only need to move in some movable furniture, without having to bother themselves.

Type A houses have one main room, one small back room, and one small kitchen. The clothes rack is installed in front of the door. Type B has two main rooms, one in front and one in the back, a small connecting room, and a small back room. It is very suitable for couples and small families with one or two children to live in.

I toured the village for more than two hours, and saw many villagers living and working leisurely, and the cleaner was cleaning up in every place.

The village faces south, with a bamboo fence wall in front of it and a river behind it. It is surrounded by fields, so every house gets sunlight.

"It's truly a small paradise outside the city!" I thought as I reluctantly walked back home.

Random Notes 162

— (Zhan Ruoye)

A friend is down on his luck in Jingkou and often sighs with emotion. One day, he wrote, "Seeing people on the streets crying from hunger and cold, I can't help but think of taking a step back." If one can take another step back, that would be true wisdom.

"White clouds seal the stone cave, tame deer nibble flowers, spring has leftovers; red rain moistens the pearl curtain, celestial birds brush trees, the ground is without dust." One need not have this realm, but reading about it is already intoxicating. Mr. Shou Juan's "Stepping on Yellow Mountain stones, one becomes a carefree immortal. Sitting on a pine-needle cushion, sleeping for a thousand years" shows that a blessed land need not be sought in heaven; it requires a wise heart to appreciate it.

Speaking and Striking the Bell 163

— Haike

Once, I visited Mr. Hu Zhantang with Fo Chang and saw a couplet written by the famous calligrapher Ma Gongyu hanging in his guest room. The couplet read: "Say what should be said at the right time, strike the bell as a monk should every day." Fo Chang jokingly asked: "Why do you hang this couplet, aren't you appointing yourself as passive? The state is like this, we should untie our hair and tie our caps in rage, who would dare to be late?" He answered: "The meaning of this couplet is precisely to be proactive and responsible, how can you call it passive? People nowadays should speak but don't, should strike the bell but don't, which is why the state affairs are getting worse every day. If one can speak in time, the words will be accurate; if one can strike the bell on time every day, nothing will be left undone. The reason why foreign countries are strong is only because everyone can speak and strike the bell." His words hit the current ills and are thought-provoking, so I record them to be a warning to the nation.

A Study of the Women's Army 164

— Sun Linchang

The international situation is gloomy on all sides, and the city is full of storms, giving the impression that something is about to happen. Thus, the "female heroes" of various countries are eager to get started and are engaging in major activities, so I am writing "A Study of the Women's Army".

The Wallets of the Master and Miss 165

— Xianghong

Niangzi is a common term for young women, and women who join the army are called the Women's Army. This originates from the Tang Dynasty, "Princess Pingyang married Chai Shao. When Gaozu first raised troops, Shao distributed his family wealth and recruited deserters across the river. The Princess led an elite force of more than ten thousand and met with the Prince of Qin north of the Wei River. Shao and the Princess each set up their own headquarters and were called the Women's Army." See the Tang Shu. Also, the Youxue Qionglin states: "The army is called Niangzi, auspicious and difficult to destroy." Today, the common people use the term Women's Army to describe women uniting and using force. For example, if a husband has an affair, his shrewish wife, due to chemical reactions, invites her girlfriends to argue. Writers often say: "The Women's Army launches a punitive expedition."

The Three Religions and Nine Classes 166

— Yilu

The phrase "three religions and nine classes" is something we often hear. But exactly what are the three religions and the nine classes? Perhaps not many people know. According to my friend: the three religions, of course, refer to Confucianism, Taoism, and Buddhism! The nine classes, however, are divided into upper, middle, and lower classes. The upper nine classes are: 1. Emperors; 2. Sages; 3. Hermits; 4. Immortals; 5. Scholars; 6. Warriors; 7. Artisans; 8. Merchants; 9. Farmers. The middle nine classes are: 1. Candidates in the Imperial Examinations; 2. Doctors; 3. Fortune Tellers; 4. Jinpi (medicine peddlers); 5. Painters; 6. Artists; 7. Monks; 8. Taoists; 9. Those skilled in qin and chess. The lower nine classes are: 1. Prison Guards; 2. Yamen Runners; 3. Weighers; 4. Nuns; 5. Matchmakers; 6. Miscellaneous Performers; 7. Those who trade in stolen goods; 8. Thieves; 9. Prostitutes. The Jinpi of the middle nine classes refers to those who tell fortunes and sell herbal medicine, and those who trade in stolen goods in the lower nine classes refers to those who buy stolen goods. But whether there are any errors or not, I still have to ask those with better knowledge!
